Flour Export Ban

Ministry of Finance Implements Revocation

Jianghai Customs Notice

Effective Immediately, Abolished

Shenshi News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance did not revoke the flour export ban when it lifted the ban on rice and wheat exports. The Shanghai Flour Trade Association petitioned the Ministry of Finance to lift the ban as an example to promote foreign trade. The association has now been ordered to approve, and the Jianghai Customs has announced the revocation of the ban. The details are as follows:

Flour Ban Lifted

The Ministry of Finance has approved the Flour Trade Association's request to allow flour exports, but the special tax will still be collected. The original approval order stated: "The ban on flour exports was originally implemented because of domestic disasters and insufficient food supplies. The Ministry was ordered to handle this matter. Now, there is a surplus of agricultural products in various regions, and the situation of sluggish sales is the opposite of what it was before. The request to lift the ban on the export of wheat flour of grades two, three, and four can be approved. However, wheat flour is not subject to customs duties. The current tax is still a special tax, which is clearly different from the customs duties levied on other grains. Therefore, a complete tax exemption cannot be granted. The special wheat flour tax shall continue to be collected as stipulated in the regulations, and half of the actually collected tax amount shall be refunded after export to encourage exports. As for bran, it is mostly used for industrial purposes, with a large volume exported annually. It has not been subject to the export ban and is of a different nature than grain. Therefore, it is difficult to grant the same tax exemption. Furthermore, the association petitioned for a tax exemption on bran exports in July of this year (the 22nd year of the Republic), and the Ministry rejected it. It should be handled in accordance with the original case. This approval is notified for information, in addition to being submitted and distributed."

Customs Notice

Yesterday, Jianghai Customs issued English notice No. 1334, abolishing the flour export ban from today. The original text is translated as follows: "Notice is hereby given that the previous ban on the export of wheat flour has now been revoked. All procedures for transporting wheat flour in various coastal areas that were originally established will be abolished from today. All other customs prices remain unchanged. This notice is issued by Tang Haian, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, and Robert L. Paddock, Inspector General of Customs."

Purchasing American Wheat Flour

Yesterday's Price Negotiations

Manufacturers Appointed Gu Xinyi and Others as Representatives

To Negotiate with the American Cotton and Wheat Management Office

Xin Xin News Agency reports that Shanghai flour manufacturers are purchasing 240,000 tons of American wheat and 6.4 million bags of American flour. On the 13th of this month, six conditions were presented and approved by the Ministry of Finance. It is reported that the flour and wheat have already arrived in Shanghai and could be shipped by the manufacturers themselves, but the unloading has been delayed due to unresolved price negotiations. A Xin Xin News Agency reporter learned that the manufacturers held a meeting on the 16th to decide on the quantity to be purchased by each factory and appointed Gu Xinyi and others as representatives to negotiate prices with Mr. Sidema, the director of the American Cotton and Wheat Management Office, yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM so that each factory can ship the goods as soon as possible.

Soybean and Rice Trade Association

Resolved to Subscribe for 50,000 Yuan in Shares

The Grain Transportation and Marketing Bureau is Actively Proceeding

A Shareholders' Meeting Will Be Held After Share Payments are Collected

Xin Xin News Agency reports that the China Grain Transportation and Marketing Bureau, organized by eight provinces and cities, was originally scheduled to hold its inaugural shareholders' meeting on the 20th of this month, but the date has been postponed because the economic conditions of the provinces are strained and payments have not been remitted. A Xin Xin News Agency reporter visited Gu Xinyi, the director of the bureau's preparatory office, yesterday morning to inquire about the bureau's recent situation. He said that the subscriptions from various provinces and cities have been affected by the poverty caused by years of disasters in the neighboring bandit areas. However, grain transportation and marketing is a pressing issue for our country, so the provinces and cities are actively planning to remit the payments within this month. As for Shanghai, progress is also being made on various fronts. The Soybean and Rice Trade Association recently convened a meeting and decided to subscribe for 50,000 yuan in shares. Other associations, such as the Miscellaneous Grains Association, will also convene meetings, and the amount of their subscriptions will be decided at that time. As for the inaugural shareholders' meeting, it can be held as soon as the share payments are collected.

Shanghai-Fujian Merchants Trading

Shanghai-Fujian Shipping Lines

Business is Quite Prosperous

For many years, Shanghai-Fujian merchants have frequently traded with each other in large quantities. This time, the Fujian Incident has affected the operations of Chinese ships, causing significant losses. It is reported that both Shanghai and Fujian merchants are actively exchanging telegrams to continue business, as the Central Army has successively recovered Yanping, Gutian, Fuzhou, and other places, and Chinese shipping companies such as China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Sanbei Steamship Company, and Ning Shao Steamship Company have gradually resumed the Shanghai-Fujian routes. Fuzhou's purchases from Shanghai are especially crowded. Therefore, ships sailing to Fuzhou and other places are fully loaded with goods, and business is very prosperous.

Two Railways' Defenses are Consolidated

There Should Be No Other Concerns

Central News Agency reports that since the train robbery on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, the public has been quite concerned about travel, especially on the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, which are centered on Shanghai, connecting the capital to the north and Hangzhou to the south. They occupy important positions politically, militarily, commercially, and culturally, and are of particular concern. According to a reporter's investigation, the railway protection troops on these routes were slightly moved during the Fujian Incident. There was a time when the station at Benniu was robbed due to thin defenses, but national troops quickly filled the position. Now, all stations and bridges along the lines are heavily guarded by stationed troops, military police, or security teams, who are working closely with railway workers to conduct strict patrols. The number of police officers on both railways has also been increased to fill vacancies and strengthen armaments, and the police chiefs personally inspect the situation at any time to provide protection. Recently, the bureau has ordered the police chiefs to pay extra attention. In addition to military police protecting the trains, a considerable number of armed police officers are also assigned to guard the trains, ensuring that there will be no other concerns.

Following the Robbery of the Puan Steamer

The Navy Dispatched Warships to Pursue and Suppress

And Ordered the Rescue of the Nine Kidnapped Passengers

The Puan Steamer is Scheduled to Arrive in Shanghai This Morning

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Co.'s Puan steamer, which operates on the Shanghai-Qingdao line, departed from Shanghai on the 13th of this month and was hijacked by pirates eighteen nautical miles north of Sheweishan outside the Wusongkou. It is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai this morning at 7:00 AM. The Navy has dispatched warships stationed in Xiamen to pursue and suppress the pirates and rescue the kidnapped passengers. The details are as follows:

Hijack

This morning, the Puan steamer was hijacked by pirates and forced to sail into the Zhaoan Bay in Fujian on the Shanghai-Guangdong line. The pirates used pre-arranged fishing boats to escape, taking nine passengers with them. The Shanghai China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's radio station received a telegram from the Puan captain yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM stating that the Puan had sailed to the Zhoushan waters in Zhejiang Province and was scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 7:00 AM this morning. It was originally intended to dock at the China Merchants North Line wharf, but it has now been decided to dock at the China Merchants Hua Line wharf in Pudong.

Warships Dispatched

After receiving news that the Puan steamer had been hijacked by pirates, the Navy Department telegraphed Xiamen to dispatch warships to Zhaoan Bay to pursue and suppress the pirates and rescue the kidnapped passengers. It also replied to the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. It is reported that the Jiangyuan warship stationed in Xiamen has been ordered to sail to Zhaoan Bay to pursue and suppress the pirates. After receiving a telegram from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Ministry of Transportation inquired about the truth from the Shanghai China Merchants Steam Navigation Company via long-distance telephone from Nanjing the night before and immediately consulted the Navy Department and the Fujian and Guangdong land and sea authorities to pursue and suppress the pirates and rescue the passengers.

Purpose of the Kidnapping

According to information gathered by a Xin Sheng News Agency reporter, the pirates' purpose in hijacking the Puan steamer was to kidnap passengers. The nine kidnapped passengers are all men. One of them is a steerage passenger who was mistakenly kidnapped. When Sun Zhenwu, the director of the China Merchants Qingdao branch, disguised himself as a crew member, the pirates mistook him for a steerage passenger, leading to the mistaken kidnapping of the steerage passenger, Mr. Zhu, who was traveling from Shanghai to Laiyang for medical treatment.

Southwest Test Flight

Will Retest Xikang

So That New Aircraft Can Be Deployed Immediately

After being detained in Vietnam due to accidentally entering Vietnamese territory, the Southwest test flight of the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) was released. Yesterday morning, after confirming the weather conditions in Kunming, the pilot, An Lisheng, and the flight director, Nie Kaiyi, flew back. It is expected to arrive in Chongqing tomorrow. It is reported that the company plans to open a flight route to Xikang Province on the border of Sichuan. After the aircraft returns to Chongqing, it will be used to retest Xikang. Then, it will return to Hankou, so that the new aircraft purchased from the United States can be formally deployed after arriving in Shanghai.

North Shanghai

Dispute Over Rice Transportation

Workers Petitioned All Night

Rice Merchants Requested Intervention

A Conflict Was Unavoidable This Morning

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the dispute over rice shoulder-carrying in North Shanghai continues. The shoulder-carrying laborers' petition to the Social Affairs Bureau the day before failed, and they only returned yesterday morning. The rice merchants submitted a response to the Social Affairs Bureau for review in accordance with the meeting's decision. The Social Affairs Bureau summoned rice merchants from North Shanghai for questioning. Details are as follows:

Petitioned for Days

Over 120 shoulder-carrying laborers from the Hongtai Yuji Shoulder-Carrying Company petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau since the morning of the day before. The bureau registered them, but more than 40 of the laborers did not match the previously reported lists. The Social Affairs Bureau refused to register them, but these workers insisted on a solution before dispersing. Until 11:05 PM the night before, they remained gathered outside the Social Affairs Bureau. The Seventh District Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau, fearing further complications, sent police to suppress them, but to no avail. They had no choice but to take them to the branch, where the chief repeatedly advised them. At 12:00 AM, they were escorted to the Jiangwan Seventh District Office. The workers had no choice but to walk back to the guildhall at Xinzha Bridge at 2:30 AM yesterday morning, arriving at 4:00 AM.

Workers' Attitude

According to Wang Dafu, the foreman of the Hongtai Shoulder-Carrying Company, speaking to a Xin Sheng News Agency reporter, the more than 40 shoulder-carrying laborers who were not registered by the Social Affairs Bureau were laborers who had registered successively, so they were not included in the reported list. All merchants include foremen currently serving, and foremen often deny shoulder-carrying laborers because of their rights. Even relatives are treated as strangers. Yesterday's merchant meeting even heard claims that the foremen have guarantees and heavy responsibilities. This point contradicts the original intention of the Social Affairs Bureau to abolish contracting. The workers are determined to take effective measures to deal with it.

Industry Representatives

Rice merchants said that these shoulder-carrying laborers were all hired by Shi Dengfu, the foreman of the Hongtai Shoulder-Carrying Company. They have no fixed occupation and are deliberately trying to cause trouble for the merchants. Furthermore, the foremen who contract the rice transportation are responsible for compensation. For example, if a worker steals rice and escapes, the foreman is responsible for compensation. This custom has been used for a long time and is not easy to abolish. Yesterday's industry meeting decided to uniformly oppose the shoulder-carrying laborers in order to seek familiarity and stability.

Submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau

The industry associations of the soybean and rice trade, rice transportation, and rice milling jointly decided at a meeting the day before to uniformly reject the shoulder-carrying laborers. If the workers continue to cause trouble, they are prepared to suspend operations to deal with the situation. Yesterday morning, they jointly submitted the process to the Social Affairs Bureau for review. The Social Affairs Bureau also summoned rice transporters from North Shanghai at 12:00 PM.

The import of artificial silk has increased daily.

Our Country Urgently Needs to Establish Factories for Self-Production

A Capital of One or Two Million Gold Can Be Used to Start the Business

Due to Water Needs, Factories Should Be Located in the Taihu Lake Basin

The New Voice Society reports that silk prices have plummeted in recent years, leading to a drastic decline, causing the rural economy to approach collapse. Farmers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have traditionally relied on silkworm rearing, cocoon sales, and silk reeling as a major source of income throughout the year. The reasons for the silk industry's failure are half due to the impact of artificial silk and half due to Japanese dumping in the United States, which has led to the occupation of overseas markets. A reporter interviewed Mr. Jiang Linshu, the manager of China New Printing and Dyeing Company, yesterday. According to him, the position of artificial silk today makes it impossible to eliminate. If countries such as Britain, the United States, Italy, and Japan establish factories to manufacture it, the quantity will be astonishing. The sales volume in Shanghai alone is as high as 400 boxes per day. Groups are promoting sales in our country's market, with fierce competition. If Chinese people do not establish factories for self-production, the outflow of money will be countless. The best raw material for manufacturing artificial silk is cotton, followed by pine trees, seaweed, and other slightly sticky plants. However, lake water is more suitable than seawater. Mr. Jiang is a giant in the silk industry. He visited Japan twice in his early years to observe their silk and artificial silk factories, carefully studying them and gaining a lot of experience. Mr. Jiang also said that he went to Japan five years ago when Japan newly established a large-scale artificial silk factory called "Asahi," with a capital of six million, half from the government and half from merchants. The factory was located on the shore of Lake Biwa. The lake is surrounded by mountains, with beautiful scenery, clean water, and waterfalls directly into the lake. The water quality is very good. When the factory opened, its machinery was also purchased from Europe and the United States, with a large scale and complete equipment. In less than a year, artificial silk from the Asahi factory was discovered in Shanghai. The Japanese are very dedicated to business, far beyond what we can match. Recently, there have been dozens of large and small artificial silk factories around Lake Biwa. Chinese merchants buy and use artificial silk, mostly from Italy and the United States. Recently, it may be difficult to avoid buying Japanese goods. Mr. Jiang spoke with great emotion and continued, saying that if our country wants to establish a factory for self-production, a capital of one or two million can be raised to start the business. Due to the water needs, the factory should be located in the Taihu Lake basin, rather than in Shanghai. Now that Chinese people are promoting domestic goods, there should be many enthusiastic and knowledgeable people in the business community. Why not quickly take action?

Representatives Jiang Shizhi and Jiang Zisheng from the Businessmen's Joint Association, the Bean and Rice Industry Shanghai North Office, and the Grain Dealers Association inquired about the situation in order to mediate.

Rice Industry Petition

The Dagong Society reports that Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Bean and Rice Trade Association of this city, Zhu Zizhen, Chairman of the Rice Milling Industry Association, Jiang Shizhi, Chairman of the Grain Dealers Association, Jiang Zisheng, Director of the Bean and Rice Industry Shanghai North Office, Lu Jingwen, and other five people went to the city center yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM to petition the municipal government, requesting a swift stop to the porters' competition for work to stabilize commerce. Secretary Feng Yuhong received them, inquired about the situation, and promised to instruct the Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus to properly handle the matter. Regarding the issue of placing unemployed workers, they will wait for detailed investigation and verification. The representatives expressed their satisfaction before returning.

Sending Police for Protection

Because the problem of placing all the unemployed porters still has no concrete solution, they will go to the rice shops and factories in the Xin Zha Bridge and Wu Zhen Road area this morning to request work. After learning of this news, the rice industry was deeply concerned that it would cause renewed disputes and affect people's livelihoods. They immediately reported to the Fourth District Headquarters of the Public Security Bureau, requesting that police be sent to protect the work. After learning the situation, District Chief Lai has notified the nearby police station to send more police officers to the rice industry docks this morning to protect the work and maintain people's livelihoods.

Party Headquarters Thorough Investigation

The Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters believes that Shi Dengfu's repeated leading of crowds to compete for porter work is a major issue for local security. Yesterday, it specifically sent Lu Yinchu, an officer from the People's Military Affairs Section, to the various rice industry groups to inquire about the situation in detail and thoroughly investigate Shi Dengfu's actions in order to take strict action.

The All-China National Goods Match Industry Joint Association previously reported that the national goods match industry was declining due to the dumping of foreign matches. Longhua Air and Sea Port Completed

The Location of the Port is Suitable, and the Area is Extremely Large

Currently Cooperating with the City Government to Develop the City

China Airlines, for the upcoming success of Sino-American Aviation, has built a grand Far East air and sea port on the waters of Longhua. Construction on the port has been underway for some time, and the flight path has now been completed. All facilities are largely complete, and it is planned to cooperate with the municipal government to operate secondary businesses. After it is successful, it can become the only air and sea port in the Far East.

A Glimpse of the Entire Port

The entire port is located near the Longhua Shanghai-Hangzhou Line station. The area was formerly the Huangpu River and later Longhua Town, with both water and land available. The location is excellent. The total area of the port is several thousand feet and has now been paved for airplanes to land. A small portion of the waterfront in front has been built into a cement gate for the purpose of stopping planes.

Building the Water and Land Port

The water port has been completed after hard work. The so-called water port is only the water surface of the Huangpu River. No ships pass through this area. A narrow water railing floats on the surface of the port, specifically for pilots to walk on and off. The land port next to this water port occupies a very large area. A narrow flight path has now been built to allow airplanes to take off into the air from the path.

Developing the City

In order to facilitate travelers and develop Longhua, the company is now planning to build upscale boarding houses, dining halls, clubs, and various entertainment facilities on the open space of the port. However, this is a major undertaking, and the economic aspect is particularly important, and it is also closely related to municipal facilities. Therefore, it has been discussed with the municipal government once, intending to cooperate fully to achieve perfection.

More than one hundred people, including Yao Xinzhi, publicly elected Qin Yanqi, the representative of the Shanghai Charity Group, as the chairman. The following important cases were resolved: (1) The date of the memorial service was decided to be March 18th at 2:00 PM. (2) The location of the memorial service was decided to be at the China Vocational Education Center. (3) The preparatory staff was designated as three groups, including the China Vocational Education Society. (4) The preparatory expenses were decided (omitted). (5) The posthumous title of Mr. Yao Zirang was publicly discussed and it was resolved to be [Gong Jing], meaning [being resolute in one's duties is called Gong, and being respectful and refraining from unnecessary speech is called Jing]. (6) Building a statue for commemoration to last forever was approved in principle. The specific plan will be solicited from various groups and discussed at the next meeting.

Women's National Goods Movement

Propaganda Rally Held Yesterday

Attended by Over Five Thousand People, Extremely Crowded

Lianhua Company Filmed on the Spot

The Women's National Goods Movement Propaganda Rally, sponsored by the First Special District Citizens' Union of this city, opened at the City Chamber of Commerce Hall yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, attended by more than five thousand ladies from all walks of life, which was a grand occasion. The details are recorded as follows.

Attending Representatives

The attendees yesterday included Wang Yansong, Ye Jiaxing, He Bingxian (Ji Zize Jin Dynasty), Lin Kecong, Shu Huizhen, Wu Zhihao, Chen Jicheng, Cao Zhigong, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Yichen, Yu Zhongxian, Chen Binghui, Yin Jialiang, Sun Mingqi, Fang Peicheng, Chen Shude, Leng Bingnan, Wang Jian'e, Zhu Baoluo, Zhu Yangwu, Tao Leqin, Ren Nongxuan, Liu Zhongying, Tan Dongshan, Zhu Zhichun, etc.

However, because the guests were crowded yesterday, and the situation was like a tide, it was difficult to maintain order, which made it impossible to receive guests separately. And those who were supposed to speak could not move forward, and left in a hurry. Therefore, it was not possible to implement the speeches and performances.

Chairman's Report

The presidium of the conference consisted of Wu Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Ye Jiaxing, Zhang Yichen, Wu Zhihao, Yu Zhongxian, Hu Fengxiang, Lin Kanghou, Chen Binghui, Wang Hanliang, Chen Jicheng, Cao Zhigong, and other twelve people. The master of ceremonies was Chen Jiufeng, and the recorder was Zheng Dongshan. After Wang Hanliang reported the purpose of the meeting, Wang Yansong, Ye Jiaxing, and He Bingxian (Ji Dynasty) delivered speeches in succession.

Wang Yansong's Speech

Wang Yansong said in his speech, "Brothers, I am participating in the Women's National Goods Movement Conference today, and I am one of the presidium. Because I have not fully understood the past preparation process, I will no longer report to you. I would like to contribute my personal views to the guests. First, today's conference is an organized movement to promote the development of national goods. All guests, regardless of men, women, old, or young, should adhere to this meaning and take a responsibility to promote national goods, set an example, and gradually promote them throughout the country. Second, the name of this association is the Women's National Goods Movement Propaganda Conference, but its meaning is broad, not narrow. Because promoting national goods is a natural duty that any of the 400 million compatriots should bear. Just because this year is designated as the Women's National Goods Year, it should be promoted by women and should not be unrelated to men. We know that saving the country through national goods is the urgent task of the moment. All compatriots should have the same goal, not let others go first, and work hard. Especially men, who have more service experience and deeper impressions in society, should understand the importance of promoting and using national goods and intensify their efforts. As for the responsibility of women, in terms of the family, all procurement and purchase matters are exclusively authoritative. In the past, various products in the family, especially cosmetics, can be said to be mostly imported. This may be due to the lack of knowledge of a few people, resulting in it. If they can take advantage of today, the Women's National Goods Year, to unanimously wake up and work hard to promote national goods, so that the effect of today's conference can be carried forward and achieve the goal of saving the country through national goods, this is what I am willing to encourage with you all."

Ye Jiaxing's Speech

Ye Jiaxing said in his speech, "At the beginning of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, we designated this year as the National Goods Year, and we have spared no effort in promotion and publicity throughout the year. But in reality, the excess of foreign goods is still increasing. To put it bluntly, the effect can be said to be very slight. Therefore, based on the experience of this failure, we believe that the promotion of national goods in the future must change its direction and start with the women's sector itself. There are two reasons for this: First, modern housekeeping, no matter how the family is organized, is controlled by women. Therefore, how to purchase food, clothing, and entertainment products is mostly determined by the housewife, and men do not have any prejudices. Therefore, if women love to use national goods, there is no reason to abandon national goods and go for foreign goods in the family. This is one reason. The other reason is that women are rich in the psychology of loving beauty, and the novelty and ostentation of foreign goods are also what those who love beauty like to pursue. And there is an unbreakable concept in society that foreign goods are exquisite and cannot be compared with national goods. This concept, if allowed to spread and expand, is actually an invisible obstacle to national goods. Therefore, we must universally publicize the beauty and applicability of national goods to the women's sector to correct their misconceptions. This is the second reason. At the same time, because women in our country have always been rich in the virtues of thrift and saving money, men's squandering of money is often enlightened by the character and influence of women. Although this trend has gradually disappeared in the cities in recent years, most can still maintain this virtue. Therefore, if women can switch to using national goods, it can indirectly create a social atmosphere of thrift and integrity for men. This is the third reason. The above is the origin of our advocacy for the women's national goods movement. I hope that the ladies will work hard, etc." Other speeches were omitted.

(5) National martial artists Ren Chaojun and Luo Ruixing's martial arts show. (6) Ren Jingju and Li Dasheng's "National Goods Song." (7) Ye Zhiyong's "Wang Wuneng's Farewell to His Wife." (10) Modern drama (Awakening), especially Zhang Xianglu and Hu Beiqi's expressions were the best.

Filming

Huaou Candy Company, China Chemical Industry Society, Huacheng, Nanyang, and other companies donated national goods items in the venue. Because there were not many items prepared, they were quickly used up. Those who came later got nothing. All entertainment was filmed by Lianhua Company for mobile news footage to promote it to various places.

Slogans

(4) Are you Chinese? Why don't you use Chinese goods? (5) Promoting national goods is to resist foreign goods. (6) Hating foreign goods is the weapon to kill us. Mayor Wu Actively Preparing

The Ministries of Finance and Industry and Commerce Plan

Maintaining Egg Sales

Negotiating with France to Reduce Egg License Tax

The Ministry of Finance Has Consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for Deliberation

Regarding the French government's amendment to the egg import license tax, the International Trade Bureau, after receiving instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, convened a meeting of Shanghai egg merchant leaders on the 29th of last month to discuss remedial measures. The New News Agency reporter visited Ji Zizejin, Director of the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, yesterday to inquire about everything. It is learned that the Bureau has summarized the meeting proposals and the opinions submitted by the Shanghai Egg Industry Association and the Jue Egg Industry Association and submitted them to the ministry for verification. The Bureau has now received instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Regarding this case, in addition to the International Trade Bureau's according to the opinions of the egg merchants, the Ministries of Finance and Industry and Commerce are actively carrying it out. The original instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the original consultation from the Ministry of Finance to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce are recorded as follows.

Instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce

Regarding the French government's amendment to the egg import license tax, on the 13th of this month, we ordered your bureau to plan remedial measures and consulted the Ministry of Finance for joint review. Now, the Ministry of Finance's reply has been received by the ministry. A copy of the original consultation is hereby issued for reference. Please be informed of this order.

Original Treasury Communication

Approved is your department's communication No. 2197 regarding commerce, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' communication concerning the French government's revised levy on egg product licenses. Your communication requested consideration and a response. Upon reviewing the case, previously received from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, it was noted that our nation's trade in chilled and wet eggs with France has been declining this year, likely due to French import restrictions and heavy taxation. This Ministry believes that maintaining sales of these products requires (1) reducing or exempting export taxes on chilled and mixed eggs, and (2) negotiating with the French government for reduced taxes on our chilled and wet eggs. The Sino-French Tariff Treaty includes reciprocal most-favored-nation clauses. Although, due to differences in the French tariff system at the time, a separate exchange of notes stated that France could not apply the lowest tariff rate to all of China, the current French tax on eggs imported from countries such as Belgium, the Netherlands, and Poland is set at one franc and fifty centimes, while the import license tax levied on eggs shipped from our country to France reaches as much as four francs and sixty centimes. This disparity significantly hinders Sino-French commerce and, in principle, does not align with the spirit of most-favored-nation treatment. Regarding the reduction or exemption of export taxes on chilled and wet eggs, this Ministry has already instructed the National Tariff Commission to review the matter when revising export tariffs. As for requesting the French government to reduce taxes on Chinese chilled and wet eggs, this has been communicated to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for consideration and action to sustain export trade, as per the previous communication. This response is for your department's reference.

Two Roads Office

Leasing of Gas-Powered Vehicles

Exclusively for accepting and delivering packages on behalf of customers

Monthly Rental: $300

The Two Roads Office, which accepts and delivers packages on behalf of customers, originally had a contract with Xie Xinggong and Jiang Jinji, the vehicle operators, stipulating a charge of ten cents per package, with a minimum fee of one dollar and fifty cents per batch. While this was convenient for merchants with numerous packages, travelers with only a few packages were deterred by the high minimum fee. To accommodate these travelers, the office negotiated with the China Gas Vehicle Company to lease a gas-powered vehicle for transporting packages. After approval from the bureau, the office and the company drafted a temporary agreement for vehicle leasing, which has been in effect since December of last year. The main points of the agreement are summarized below: (1) The office temporarily leases a one-and-a-half-ton gas-powered vehicle from the company, paying a monthly rental of $300. (2) All costs, including the driver, fuel, motor oil, vehicle tax, and repairs, are borne by the company. (3) The vehicle's working hours are from 8:00 AM to 8:00 PM daily. If there is a backlog of packages, the hours may be extended to 10:00 PM. (4) If the vehicle is damaged and unusable, the office may hire another vehicle and deduct ten dollars from the monthly rental. (5) The company's gas-powered vehicle must be parked at a suitable location for immediate service and may not engage in other business activities outside of the office's delivery services. (6) The company's driver and other laborers must assist the office's personnel in loading and unloading packages. (7) This agreement is for a trial period of three months. If effective, a formal long-term contract will be established.

Wireless Radio

"Peter Pan" Trademark Lawsuit

One party accuses the other of trademark infringement

The other party claims the goods come from the same source

Chen Junsheng, the manager of the Tongtai Trading Company on Sijing Road, has recently retained attorney Lin Yingqing to file a lawsuit in the criminal court of the First Special District Court against Wang Gentang, the manager of the Meisheng Wireless Radio Company on Zhifu Road, and Li Wenxiang and Wu Xinghao, shareholders of the Lianhua Company on Beijing Road, for counterfeiting "Peter Pan" five-tube wireless radio trademarks and selling counterfeit goods. The lawsuit also includes a civil claim for an injunction and compensation of $9,000.

Defendants Li and Wu were summoned and appeared in court with their attorney, Wu Linkan. Plaintiff Chen Junsheng stated that the Tongtai Trading Company sells "Peter Pan" brand wireless radios, which are manufactured in the United States. The company registered the "Peter Pan" trademark with the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry in accordance with Article 1 of the Trademark Law in the 20th year of the Republic, receiving Registration Certificate No. 19763 on February 20th of the 22nd year of the Republic, granting exclusive rights for twenty years from December 15th of the 21st year of the Republic. Defendant Wang Gentang is counterfeiting "Peter Pan" wireless radios, selling them in the market, and advertising them widely, deceiving the public for profit. After a letter of warning was sent, Wang replied that the Lianhua Company, owned by defendants Li and Wu, had entrusted him with the sales. Therefore, the three defendants are jointly committing a crime, and since the counterfeit goods entered the market, the plaintiff's business has been greatly affected, with sales declining by several hundred units, resulting in a loss of approximately $9,000. Chen requested a judgment for compensation of losses, and presented the registration certificate and other evidence. Wang Gentang testified that Li and Wu had entrusted him to sell these wireless radios, a total of twenty-six units, priced at eighty-five dollars each, with Wang receiving a commission of five dollars per unit. Fifteen units have been sold. Li and Wu, through their attorney Wu Linkun, argued that on October 20th of last year, the Lianhua Company, through the introduction of American commercial consul Kerr of the American Consulate in Shanghai, was informed of "Peter Pan" radios, which were inexpensive and of good quality, selling for only twelve and a half US dollars. Lianhua sent a letter to the American Foreign Trade Society, ordering fifty wireless radio sets and sending a deposit, requesting immediate shipment to Shanghai. The "Peter Pan" radios are produced by the American Sackson factory and have been sold abroad for several years. After the Sackson factory closed down, all of its products were entrusted to the Foreign Trade Society for consignment sales. Lianhua Company received forty-six "Peter Pan" radios shipped from the United States by the Society. Twenty-six units were entrusted to the Meisheng Wireless Radio Company for consignment sales, and the remaining twenty units have also been sold. "Peter Pan" is not the plaintiff's trademark, as the "Peter Pan" mark was already marked on the radios when Lianhua ordered them from the United States, and the defendants did not counterfeit it. Moreover, these radios are from the same manufacturer as those sold by the plaintiff, with no difference, so there is no trademark counterfeiting. A letter was presented from Zhang Jinsheng, a comprador at the French barracks.

Jumping into Xiaobang, Falsely Reporting Kidnapping

Due to financial difficulties, this desperate measure was taken.

The truth was revealed after interrogation by the police.

Zhang Jinsheng, a native of this county residing at No. 72 La Fei De Road, La Fei Fang, French Concession, has been working as a comprador at the French military camp in Shanghai for three years. Due to financial difficulties, he was unable to pay the accounts of various businesses. On the eighth of this month, he took a chartered car to the Bund of Renji Road, instructed the driver to wait, and then went north to the North Railway Station, taking the 11:00 PM night train to Hangzhou. On the evening of the eleventh, he returned to Shanghai, but instead of going home, he stayed temporarily at a house in Hongqiao, west of Shanghai. The next morning, he secretly jumped into the Xiaobang River in Hongqiao. After waiting for a moment, he climbed back to the shore and reported to the First Police Station of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, falsely claiming that he was suddenly kidnapped by three bandits on the Bund of Renji Road on the eighth. One of the bandits had a pistol and bound him, and the $2,400 in cash in his pocket was also robbed and hidden. After about four days, the bandits brought him out and threw him into the river. After climbing out, he came to report. The police believed him and sent him home. The Lujiawan police station had previously received a report from Zhang's wife that her husband was missing. Since he had returned home, they sent an investigator to investigate. Zhang still lied about being kidnapped and claimed that he felt unwell due to excessive fear and needed to go to Guangci Hospital for medical treatment. Yesterday, the police heard that Zhang had been discharged from the hospital and, considering the seriousness of the case, went to investigate again. Zhang still insisted that he had been kidnapped. The investigators, noting that the incident occurred in the Public Concession, took Zhang to the General Police Station to report. After questioning by Chinese Inspector Li Yidong and Detective Zhang Xiaolin, many inconsistencies were found. Under strict questioning, Zhang finally revealed the truth. The investigators had him write a confession. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu explained the circumstances and requested that he be punished for false reporting under Article 182 of the Criminal Law. Zhang Jinsheng confessed that due to recent financial difficulties, he was unable to pay his accounts and used the $2,400 given by the military camp for other purposes. To save face, he fabricated the kidnapping and robbery to request an extension of time for payment from the businesses, seeking leniency, and hired attorney Fan Gang to defend him. Judge Wu Xiangzu, after reviewing the confession, determined that Zhang's actions constituted occupational embezzlement, which was not under the jurisdiction of this summary court, and ordered the case transferred to the local court for trial.

Letters and various evidence, etc.

The judge ruled that the case still required investigation and ordered the three defendants to leave and wait for further review in seven days.

Japanese Merchants

Dumping Hydrogenated Oil

Chinese Soap Manufacturers Compete to Purchase in Bulk

The Initial Enthusiasm Has Passed, A Sigh of Regret

Chinese-made soap traditionally uses tallow, pine tar, coconut oil, and other materials as manufacturing raw materials. These types of materials are produced in large quantities in various counties of Jiangsu Province. Because the soap made from them is widely used, the sales of raw materials are also very brisk. In recent years, Japanese merchants, recognizing that soap is a daily necessity, have invented a type of hydrogenated oil, also known as fish oil wax, which can be used as a substitute raw material for soap production. They import it into the Chinese market and dump it at low prices. However, the soap made from this material has very little effect. It not only cannot wash away greasy dirt, but it is also difficult to remove slight stains. Even though the selling price is low, only one or two small factories use it. Therefore, the position of domestically produced raw materials is not affected in the slightest. Recently, however, the boycott movement has effectively stalled, and Japanese merchants are taking the opportunity to transport various inferior goods to China as much as possible. Moreover, all goods are being sold at reduced prices. The price of hydrogenated oil is particularly low. Only small factories with weak capital occasionally purchased it in the past, but now the scope is larger. Soap factories with long-standing reputations are also eagerly purchasing it in bulk because they are greedy for its cheap price. They know that the soap produced will have reduced effectiveness, but they are all eager for immediate profits, and would rather abandon the excellent domestic raw materials and compete to use inferior goods. This is truly regrettable. It is hoped that there are still true advocates of domestic goods among the soap industry, and they should pay attention to this matter and not allow domestically produced soap to have only a false reputation.

The Victim Discovers a Fake Gun

A Thief Caught on the Spot

The victim saw through the deception and shouted to catch the thief.

Neighbors bravely assisted in capturing one of them.

At the home of Mao Jinhua, located at No. 13 Chunde Lane, Lanwei Road, French Concession, three bandits suddenly arrived around 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. They knocked on the door and entered, holding a fake pistol (made of rotten bananas) to threaten the victim. When they were robbing the victim of the gold watch and gold chain he was wearing, the victim saw through the fake gun and shouted "Robbers!" Chen Chusheng, who lived with him, arrived to help apprehend one of the bandits, Ren Alin, while the others escaped. The victim's right hand was scratched by Ren and bled. The police arrived and took Ren to the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the Second Special Court. First, the police lawyer stated that the case still required investigation and requested a postponement. Judge Wang granted the postponement and ordered the defendant to be detained.

Among the Seven Criminals in the Sun Jiabao Kidnapping Case

Only One Was Severely Sentenced

Zheng Wenxiang Remains the Main Perpetrator in the Case

Zheng's Wife, Concubines, and Apprentices Were All Found Not Guilty

Sun Wangshun's biological son, Jiabao, aged six, who resided at No. 115 Run'an Lane, Ximen Road, French Concession, was kidnapped on May 20th of the previous year. Successive ransom letters were received, demanding a price of $8,000, later reduced to $4,000. Negotiations failed, and the case was discovered by detectives of the French police. Seven individuals related to the case were arrested: Zhang Shuchuan, and suspects Biao Yaoshan, Zheng Loushi, Zheng Zhoushi, Zhou Wenying, Li Ziqing, and Min Xinhao. They were sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation. Zhang Shuchuan, a native of Jiangbei, confessed that he worked as a sweeper in Run'an Lane. The plaintiff's son was actually kidnapped by Zheng Wenxiang, who is still at large. After the kidnapping, Zhang was responsible for looking at the ransom ticket and writing letters. Unfortunately, the child died of illness, and the body was abandoned on Zhongshan Road, where it cannot now be found. Qiu and the others testified that although they lived with the plaintiff, they did not participate in the kidnapping. After the defense concluded, yesterday's sentencing date arrived. Judge Li sentenced Zhang Shuchuan to sixteen years of imprisonment for jointly engaging in extortion, with the number of days of pretrial detention deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. The other six individuals, including Qiu, were found not guilty.

Dense Fog and Shallow Water

Yangtze River Ships Blocked from Entering Port

Heavy Fog

Yesterday, the mouth of the Yangtze River and the outer waters of Wusong were suddenly enveloped in heavy fog, making navigation difficult. As the river water is currently receding, navigation on the Yangtze River is more challenging. The heavy fog has made the passage of river vessels even more difficult. The Wuhu and Lianhe, regular Yangtze River ships of the British firm Taikoo Yihwa, were scheduled to arrive from Hankou yesterday. Due to the fog at the mouth of the Yangtze River, the shipowners, for safety reasons, did not dare to sail early and temporarily anchored on the river, so they did not come to Shanghai. They have notified the Shanghai office that they will sail to Shanghai after the fog clears. Several other Yangtze River ships have also been delayed by the fog and have not yet arrived in Shanghai.

Shallow Water

The river water is receding and continuing to decline rapidly. The Jianghan Customs has issued a warning, notifying the six companies in Shanghai that Yangtze River ships loading goods and passengers in Shanghai for Hankou must not exceed a draft of eleven feet from yesterday onwards. Currently, the maximum draft in the Yangtze River is only twelve feet and one inch in the Jiujiang section, and only eleven feet in other areas. Exceeding this limit will make it impossible to navigate. All shipping companies have loaded cargo according to the limit. The Sanbei Company has dispatched the Sanbei shallow water vessel to Shanghai to facilitate the transportation of goods and passengers on the Shanghai-Hankou route during the shallow water season.

Freight Rates

During the shallow water season, Yangtze River vessels typically increase freight rates by twenty to thirty percent. With the current drop in river water, vessels cannot load as much cargo, resulting in significant losses. Yangtze River merchants have been calling various shipping bureaus for several days to inquire about whether shallow water fees will be increased. As Taikoo has not yet indicated its position on this matter, other Yangtze River vessels have not been able to increase prices independently. It is now reported that the shipping companies have inquired with Taikoo whether prices should be raised.

Saving a Ship

The Zhaoshang's Emei vessel, which was wrecked on the Huatanzi Reef in Fuzhou, was severely damaged again after being repaired. The total cost of repairs has reached 100,000 yuan. Recently, the bureau received a telegram from the shipowner, Ji Qingrong, stating that the upper reaches of the river have experienced a sharp decline in water levels, making the Emei vessel even more dangerous. The ship's hull is high and dry on the riverbank reefs and urgently needs to be repaired in a timely manner; otherwise, it will be beyond repair. The bureau has borrowed 20,000 yuan from the insurance company that insured the vessel to cover the cost of rescuing the Emei vessel and will remit the funds to Chongqing for rescue efforts upon arrival.

Establishment Meeting of the Beggar Relief Association

Shanghai is a major trading port in our country, and vagrants and beggars are more numerous here than elsewhere. The aggressive ones demand money at the door, while the weak ones wail along the road. This not only tarnishes international views but also disrupts social order and affects the national livelihood and people's well-being. The Shanghai Beggar Relief Association, recognizing this, is planning to eliminate beggars in the city in the spirit of human mutual assistance and the principle of division of labor. It is reported that since the preparation of the association, everything has been ready, and the inaugural meeting will be held at the Local Association at the end of this month.

Increase of Municipal Tax on Two Teahouses

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter Requesting Investigation and Rectification

Should be calculated based on one-fourth of the rent as a principle

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter yesterday to the Public Works Department and the First District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' United Association regarding the municipal general tax on the Nanjing Road Yile Tian and Tong Yuchun teahouses. The following is a transcript:

To the Public Works Department:

We have received a letter from the First District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' United Association, stating, "[Recently, our member stores, the Nanjing Road Yile Tian and Tong Yuchun teahouses, sent a joint letter stating, "We are writing to you regarding the Public Works Department's forced increase of the tax on our stores last winter. We are deeply grateful for the righteous assistance of your association and the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association. After repeated discussions with the tax office staff, we accepted the proposal in the interest of avoiding trouble. Yile Tian (No. 513 Nanjing Road) increased its annual tax by $1,400 on a rent of $4,000, and Tong Yuchun (No. 463 Nanjing Road) increased its annual tax by $1,000 on a rent of $4,400. It would be difficult for our business to bear any further tax increases, so we reluctantly agreed to the mediation and paid quarterly. However, it was agreed at the time that there would be no further increases. In a short time, the previous agreement was still fresh in our minds, but the Public Works Department insisted on achieving its assessment goals. On January 5th of the 23rd year of the Republic, before collecting the tax, the tax collector increased the estimated annual rent of Yile Tian to $7,500 by adding $2,100, and increased the tax bill of Tong Yuchun by another $840, totaling $6,240 annually. Under these circumstances, in terms of reason and logic, it is difficult for us to maintain our business in this era of agricultural and commercial bankruptcy and declining market. In terms of legal principle, the forced increase of rent and the exceeding of the due tax amount is difficult to bear. Therefore, we did not pay the increase at the time. On January 8th, the Public Works Department tax office summoned our manager and insisted on the increase. Our manager could not withstand the pressure and requested your association for assistance. We are grateful for your concern, etc.," and attached two rent receipts to the association. On January 7th of the 22nd year of the Republic, there was a forced tax increase, and our association sent a letter to your department to strongly protest the matter. Unfortunately, the manager of the teahouse was under environmental pressure at the time and was induced by the Public Works Department tax office to agree to an increase of $1,400 in the estimated rent for Yile Tian and an annual increase of $1,000 for Tong Yuchun without reporting to our association. According to the letter, the Public Works Department is becoming increasingly greedy and wants to increase the tax again, which is an insatiable desire. Moreover, the attached rent receipts show that Yile Tian's monthly rent is $335, totaling $4,020 annually, and Tong Yuchun's monthly rent is $340, totaling $4,080 annually. According to the one-fourth tax rule, Yile Tian should only pay $562.80 annually, and Tong Yuchun should only pay $571.20. The rent amount on the rent receipts is consistent with the company's accounts and is not fictitious. According to the manager of the company, the annual value of Yile Tian has been assessed at $4,000, and Tong Yuchun at $4,400 for the past six or seven years. After the forced increase last year, it is now being forcibly increased by more than half and more than one-fifth, which is enough to make the taxpayers feel disheartened. It has long been stipulated that the tax should be collected according to the proportion of rent. In recent years, the Public Works Department has forcibly increased the value of land and houses to increase its income, directly creating a few wealthy people and indirectly causing social concerns. Your association is actively trying to remedy the situation, and our association is also striving to promote rent reduction. However, the Public Works Department, which is responsible for maintaining law and order, only knows how to extract taxes through such high pressure, making citizens uneasy in their business. The association, as the representative organization of citizens and merchants, cannot remain silent. We hereby request your department to promptly advocate to the Public Works Department to exempt the two teahouses from the tax increase and reduce the tax in accordance with the standard calculation of the actual rent value to protect commerce and demonstrate fairness." We have reviewed the matter and found that the municipal general tax should be calculated based on one-fourth of the actual rent, which is an objective and concrete principle. Violating this principle and overestimating the amount is a tax increase, and its violation of the public opinion of the taxpayers cannot be concealed and should be corrected. In short, unless it can be legally proven that the rent of the teahouses is not real, the municipal general tax should be based on the rent amount stated on the rent receipts provided by the two teahouses; otherwise, it is legally unreasonable. We request your department to investigate and order the correction of this error.

To the First District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' United Association:

We have received your letter of January 10th regarding the Public Works Department of the Public Concession increasing the estimated rent and increasing the municipal general tax on the Tong Yuchun and Yile Tian teahouses. The municipal general tax on rented houses should be calculated based on one-fourth of the actual rent, which is an objective and concrete principle. Violating this principle and overestimating the amount is a tax increase, and its violation of the public opinion of the taxpayers goes without saying. If the rents of the two teahouses are not falsely reported, then the previous recognition of the estimated rent was a waiver of due rights. Anyone who handles tax collection, regardless of who they are, always considers more revenue to be paramount, so they cannot act freely. Only the balance of the law can be relied upon. The two teahouses are unaware of this legal balance and only seek peace in the present, resulting in the fulfillment of an obligation that should not be fulfilled and bringing trouble upon themselves. In addition to sending a letter to the Public Works Department requesting investigation and correction, we are replying to your request for reference.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables a Request

Reduce Telegram Fees for Encrypted Foreign Language Messages

Change to Charging 60% of the Original Price

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Ministry of Communications, Nanjing: "To the esteemed Ministry of Communications, Nanjing, This case arises from a letter from the Shanghai Banking Association stating that a letter from our member, the Bank of China, reports that foreign language encrypted telegrams have traditionally been charged at two jiao per word, with each word consisting of ten code units. Since September of last year, when the International Telegraph Union formulated new telegraph rules in Madrid, Spain, the ten-code system has been abolished, and a five-code system has been adopted, with each word charged at 60% of the original price. The current Ministry of Communications has issued an order to all telegraph offices, mandating that all domestic foreign language encrypted telegrams should also be processed in the same manner from January 1st of this year. However, regarding the charging issue, each word is still charged at the full rate of two jiao, failing to comply with the international charter and reducing the charge by 60%. Given the current economic downturn, even following the international method would increase costs by 20% compared to the old system. Charging two jiao per word now effectively doubles the fee, which is not conducive to alleviating the difficulties of businesses. This matter concerns the entire business community, and it is proposed that your esteemed association discuss with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and request the Ministry of Communications to avoid discrimination against domestic foreign language encrypted telegrams and uniformly reduce charges according to the international new charter to avoid partiality and ensure fairness. Upon approval of this, our executive committee resolved to present this directly to the Ministry of Communications. As this matter concerns the entire business community, we request your esteemed association to take charge, and also present it to the Ministry to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and uniformly reduce charges to avoid partiality and ensure fairness, etc.' Upon receiving this, we have investigated and found that since the International Telegraph Union changed the standard for foreign language encrypted telegrams to five code units per word and charged each word at 60% of the original price, your ministry has uniformly adopted these standards, which is consistent with the international telegraphic community. However, the charging system still follows the old standard of two jiao per word, exceeding the international rate by 40%, and the handling is not fair. Therefore, we are telegraphing to report the situation and respectfully request your esteemed ministry to review and approve a reduction in charges to maintain business and avoid partiality. We are deeply grateful." Signed, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Revision by the Ministry of Finance

Regulations on Penalties in Stamp Tax Ordinance

Right to Appeal to the Court Within Five Days if Dissatisfied with the Ruling

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday notified various industry associations that on the 12th of this month, they received a public letter No. 184 from the Jiangsu Stamp and Tobacco Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, stating that "In accordance with Instruction No. 1822 of the Ministry of Finance, it has been found that according to Article 4 of the current Regulations on Penalties and Enforcement of the Provisional Stamp Tax Ordinance, judicial organs are not allowed to file objections to rulings on penalties under the Provisional Stamp Tax Ordinance. Therefore, even if a ruling is inappropriate, no appeal can be filed against it. Although, according to Interpretation No. 571 of the Judicial Yuan, it is possible to request the judicial organ to issue another ruling to revoke the original ruling, there is no further recourse if the judicial organ considers that it should not be revoked. Since the implementation of this policy, there have been obstacles, and there are many such cases in the Shanghai Special District Court, which must be remedied quickly. The ministry, in conjunction with the Ministry of Judicial Administration, has revised Article 4 of the regulations into two items: The first item states that an appeal against the ruling in Article 2 may be filed with the competent superior court within five days. The second item states that no further appeal may be filed against the ruling of the appellate court. Regarding stamp tax evasion cases, if the penalty is imposed by the Special District Court within the Special District, the penalized merchant should comply with the provisions of the revised Article 4 and file an appeal within the specified time limit if he believes that the original ruling is inappropriate. In addition to the Tax Affairs Office instructing the Shanghai Concession Cigarette Inspection Office to take note, the revised rules are copied and sent to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to notify merchants to take note." A copy of the attached rules was received, and accordingly, the revised rules are copied and sent to you for your information. Please also notify the merchants to take note. Included is a copy of the revised Regulations on Penalties and Enforcement of the Provisional Stamp Tax Ordinance by Judicial Organs. Upon receiving this, it was found that the public associations, such as the rental car industry, have repeatedly sent letters stating that there is no appeal mechanism for stamp tax penalties in the Special District, and merchants are suffering. We have previously requested relief based on the regulations. Now, with the aforementioned approval, the original rules are printed and circulated for your information. Please check and forward them to your subordinates for their information. This is essential. End of statement."

Six Abducted Men and Women Uncovered in Dinghai

After investigation, the procuratorate found that there were six abducted men and women, mostly abducted from Shanghai. Therefore, in addition to sending separate letters to the local courts to summon family members and issuing a public notice to claim them, Song sent the previous situation and photos of the six children to Wen Hongen, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, yesterday, requesting him to issue a public notice to claim them. It is reported that Director Wen reviewed the letter and, for the sake of reuniting the children with their families, immediately instructed Yin Guanzhi, Director of the Relief Section of the Second Division of the bureau, to handle the matter. The names, ages, and origins of the six men and women abducted in Shanghai are as follows: (1) Jin Aliang, male, eight years old, from Hangzhou, living in Houcao, father's name is Yi Ji, selling zongzi at Hangzhou Railway Station. (2) Liu Luhai, also known as Lu Huating, male, six years old, from Shandong (also said to be from Yangzhou), living at No. 3 Kangti Road, French Concession, Shanghai, father earns a living by pushing a cart. (3) Zhou Qixiang, male, five years old (also said to be seven years old), from Changzhou, living inside the South Gate of Changzhou (also said to be No. 5, the second house in Xujia Lane, Nanjing Road, Shanghai), father's name is Tutu (also said to be Zhou Zifan), working as an accountant in a Guanghuo store in Gaoqiao, Pudong. (4) A girl surnamed Gao, name unknown, seven years old, from Jiangbei, living in Changqiao, Shanghai, father works as a rickshaw puller. (5) A four-year-old boy (also said to be named A Mao), from Ningbo. (6) Song Xiaomao, male, eight years old (also said to be from Shandong), living at No. 7 Kangti Road, French Concession, Shanghai, father's name is Tu Fu Fang, pushing a cart, older brother's name is Xiao Afu, carrying water for watering flowers.

Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau Establishes a South Shanghai Office

Site Determined at the Original Site of the Municipal Party Headquarters

Since the Municipal Health Bureau moved to the new urban area, it is concerned that the densely populated South Shanghai area may be difficult to reach with health facilities. Therefore, it plans to establish a South Shanghai Office in the South Shanghai area. The original site of the Municipal Party Headquarters has been determined as the office location, and preparations are underway. It is expected to officially start operations in early March. Chung Hwa Book Company

Reprint of Sibu Beiyao

The Sibu Beiyao previously published by the Chung Hwa Book Company on Jing'an Temple Road has carefully selected books, excellent printing, and the antique and moving imitation Song Dynasty movable type, which can be compared with the fine prints of the Ming and Qing dynasties imitating the Song Dynasty. It is especially praised by readers. Both pre-sale reservations were fully subscribed and closed. Recently, there have been many more requests, and some have even sought to purchase at higher prices but have not been able to obtain them. The company should have reprinted it immediately, but it is quite laborious due to the large number of volumes. Therefore, for the sake of circulating ancient books, it has decided to reprint them. A special kind of Lian Shi paper has been ordered from the Jiangnan and Baoshan paper mills. The size has been changed to five Kai large format, and the space between the lines has been widened. The book is of a large format and is sold in groups for pre-order to satisfy the wishes of book collectors at home and abroad.

Yongtai Silk Factory Recruits Silkworm Farmers

The Yongtai Silk Factory in Wuxi was founded by Mr. Xue Shouhuan. Mr. Xue has traveled in Europe for many years and has a wealth of knowledge and experience in sericulture. Recently, he was deeply saddened by the disastrous defeat of China's silk industry, which was almost unable to stand in the European and American markets. To reverse the decline, thorough reforms are necessary. Therefore, in recent years, he has hired domestic sericulture experts to preside over the factory affairs and has added a sericulture training class to train professionals. He has also sent experts to England, America, France, Italy, Japan, and other countries to investigate the sales and production of silk. This spring, he plans to set up silkworm farming cooperatives in the areas with the most mulberry production to guide farmers in silkworm farming knowledge in order to improve the products. Therefore, the need for talent is extremely urgent. Those with considerable experience in silkworm farming guidance, regardless of gender, must be recruited. Those who are interested in this can go to the factory on January 25 to discuss the matter.

Jin Yidan's Invention of Thermal Bottles

China's thermal bottle industry has been very developed in recent years, but unfortunately, it still adheres to the old methods and uses silver powder for manufacturing, resulting in weak reflectivity and failure to compete with imported products. Although some have switched to using colored glass liners, the products are far from satisfactory. Recently, it has been heard that Mr. Lin Zeren, director of the Tianjie Chemical Laboratory at No. 54 Nanjing Road, has taken this into account and has carefully researched and invented the manufacture of gold-colored bottle liners, which are much better than the silver liners currently used by factories. Its heat preservation ability is more durable than silver liners, and because of its stronger reflectivity, the amount of liquid stored in the bottle can be seen clearly. The heat preservation ability of those using gold liners can be increased to 36 hours. Therefore, this invention is indeed a major revolution in the thermal bottle industry. Mr. Lin has already applied to the Ministry of Industry for a patent, and it is also heard that several factories are currently negotiating. It is expected that these high-quality thermal bottles will be launched soon.

Continental American Company

To Establish a Branch in Shanghai

Contribution of the Latest Model of Grain Storage Machine

The Continental American Company is a company specializing in the foreign wheat business. The company has huge capital and perfect equipment. There are branches in various European countries. Because it is aware that the sales of foreign wheat in our country are extensive, it has specially sent Mr. Leon Hakim to China to investigate and appointed him as the General Manager of Shanghai. He is currently residing in Room 701 of the Metropole Hotel at the intersection of Sima Road and Jiangxi Road as a temporary office. A formal office will be established soon. According to Mr. Hakim, the general office will build a new-style wheat storage machine in Washington and Vancouver. The function of the machine is to change the old-style packaging storage method to bulk storage and can be permanently preserved. The cost is approximately US$1 million. The capacity of this machine can store 2 million bushels of wheat, making it the world's largest storage facility. This project has now hired 300 to 350 workers to start construction. At the earliest, it can be completed by July. If the progress is slow, it can also be extended by three or four months. The greatness of the project can be imagined.

Huahui gambling is extremely harmful. Although the Municipal Police Department has been closely investigated, it has not been successful. Re-trial and Verdict on the Human-Dog Intercourse Case

Chen Xinzhai and Others Sentenced to More Than Nine Years Imprisonment

Chen Xinzhai, a Henan man who used to ring the bell at the Yong'an Company amusement park, and his mistress, Chen Lu, were arrested and sent to the First Special Court for trial and sentencing after raising a black dog and four young girls at No. 12 Hongfu Lane, Xinzha Road, and performing human-dog intercourse at major hotels. Chen and Lu were sentenced to ten years and two months of imprisonment each. Chen and others were dissatisfied and appealed to the Second Branch Court, which upheld the original verdict. They then appealed to the Supreme Court in Nanjing, but because part of the case was not yet clear, it was sent back for re-trial. The Second Branch Court of the High Court concluded the re-trial last Wednesday. Zhang Tianyin, a lawyer from the police department, appeared in court and requested that the original verdict be upheld and the appeal be dismissed. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, the date for the verdict of this case arrived. The police department proposed Chen Xinzhai and Chen Lu from the prison. Zhao Zhengtao presented it with the two judges, Xie Jiang and Zhou, to the court and announced the verdict. Chen Xinzhai was sentenced to nine years and ten months of imprisonment and fined 310 yuan. Chen Lu was sentenced to nine years and eight months of imprisonment and fined 320 yuan as a warning.

▲ Advantages of Domestic Warm Spring Stove: Meifeng Metal Casting Factory has recently produced a type of stove named the "1923-style Coal-Saving Warm Spring Stove." It boasts an artistic exterior and scientific interior, making it the most valuable new product among domestic goods. Since its launch, orders from various sectors have been extremely enthusiastic, with demand exceeding supply. It is heard that the factory is working day and night to increase production and has added sample rooms at the Nanjing Road Family Industrial Society and the Jiangxi Road China Pottery Company to fulfill its original intention of promoting domestic goods and resisting foreign imports. The stove has a beautiful appearance, resembling ancient bronze vessels, and can serve as a high-quality decorative item for interiors. Its embossed patterns further enhance heat transfer, allowing for even distribution of heat, surpassing any other stove. The interior uses pressure-treated bituminous coal with curved ventilation, allowing heat to naturally accumulate within the stove, which is unprecedented in any other stove. It truly showcases ingenious craftsmanship and enhances the glory of domestic goods. If this spirit is maintained, the factory's future is truly limitless.

▲ Natural Lump Coal to Replace Coal Balls: To recover its rights and interests, the Shanghai Suili Coal Company directly extracts and transports domestic Liujiang white coal, carefully selecting clean, uniformly sized lumps equal to coal balls. These are packed in bamboo baskets for use as a substitute for coal balls. They have strong firepower, very light ash residue, the convenience of coal balls without taking up space, and none of the drawbacks of yellow soil forming the balls. Initially, the price is set lower than any white coal or coal balls. All those who purchase a full ton will receive a free stove or a basket of large charcoal as an incentive.

▲ Zhu Hesheng Leather Trunk Factory Establishes Distribution Center: Zhu Hesheng Leather Trunk Factory, located at 113 East Street inside Shanghai's Xiaodongmen, has been in business for over seventy years. Film

▲ "Power and Glory" Screens at the Grand Shanghai: The Grand Shanghai Theater, located at Xizang Road, Nanjing Road North, is screening Fox Company's extraordinary film "Power and Glory" starting today. The content is insightful and outstanding, making it a unique feature of American cinema. The entire film uses a narrative method, which is an innovation since the advent of sound films. It depicts a virtuous wife as gentle and considerate, and a good man as arrogant, abandoning the old and embracing the new. Movie lovers should be quick to see it.

Reading Questions and Answers

Reading Plan (I)

Reading Guidance...

After receiving your department's registration certificate, I truly felt indescribable joy. I only waited for the sky to darken quickly, to quickly pass ten o'clock, so that my work could be released. I can freely review the mistakes I made during my solitary self-study journey in the past, I want to honestly confess, and I also want to follow the procedures of your department's research, draft a plan, and make the first communication.

Alas! Things are really unlucky, tonight it happens to be my turn to pack copper coins, after ten o'clock, I am still packing one envelope after another. This work continued until twelve o'clock, which really killed me, the store's rules are that after one o'clock all staff must go to bed, otherwise they will not be able to get out of bed tomorrow, and will be punished.

Sir! I am now continuing to write. The time is twenty-four hours apart, it is the second night's ten forty-five, tonight I can finish this communication.

Sir! Do you think the above small talk can be taken away! No! Absolutely not! This is my actual life, the actual life of an apprentice. You must know this first, in order to understand my requirements, in order to give me the food that I can possibly swallow, in order for me to receive your department's teachings; at the same time, your work will not be in vain!

I am so busy. Ten hours of regular life every day, not including the chores that are not part of the regular work, are determined by the managers and supervisors, it is an [unwritten] code, you cannot predetermine it. However, I pay attention to all aspects of life... I save wasted time with agility, flexibility, and organization, and fill in non-[work-related services,] so I still have two or three hours of extra free time every day to use for reading. I am always tense, so even when reading I want to use the least amount of time and energy to get the greatest effect.

I believe this effort is possible, but I have not yet obtained what method should be taken for this effort?

My previous self-study was mostly biased towards Chinese, so I have made some progress in writing. Last year, I saw many people talking about social science in newspapers and magazines, and I also wanted to find some to read, and later I borrowed some from former classmates. But I immediately encountered two difficulties, the first was that I couldn't understand it, and the second was that the books were too thick, making it inconvenient to read a few pages in one night. Because it is not like a novel, you can put it down today and continue reading tomorrow night, the plot is not easy to pick up, this kind of book is already difficult to understand, once you put it down, the next day you have to read it from the beginning. Otherwise, you can't read it down. I used extraordinary patience, but the result was still limited. So, I asked my friend to borrow thinner, more popular books, he laughed and said... [There aren't any in China]. In the end, I still had to read with a stiff neck, read, although I did manage to finish them one by one, but the price I paid was too high. (To be continued)
