(1) Overture

Because the stones from other hills can polish jade, in this Chinese Women's National Goods Year, let us see how other people are acting. Ladies and gentlemen, these are trifles, but hopefully those who speak are unintentional, and those who listen are intentional!

The American prohibition has been lifted under the Blue Eagle policy. However, the beer that Americans drink, the beer they make themselves, has a larger market than French champagne.

The mysterious woman Jia Bao, on her last return to her country after leaving the United States, passed through France. Parisian merchants were prepared to do a lot of business, but in the end, she did not buy a single thing. She returned empty-handed from a mountain of treasure. The clever French goods never managed to exchange for the money of this Swedish girl.

It is said that after Japanese girls marry far away to China, many Japanese housewives still can't forget Japan (of course, there are exceptions). The most obvious proof is that they will set up a home for you with purely Japanese-made appliances.

The Development After the Reorganization of the Huada Handkerchief Factory

— Zhen

Since our country was forced open by the great powers with cannons, it has been followed by economic invasion, with goods arriving in a continuous stream. Our fat and cream have been sucked dry. The September 18th Incident occurred, and the national situation became as precarious as a pile of eggs. If we do not rise up to seek survival, even if we do not perish in the cannons, we will still perish in the chronic economic invasion! Cantonese people Wang Zijia, Xiao Guihong, Wang Yulin, Ma Fan, Huang Qin and other gentlemen, feeling the responsibility that everyone has for the rise and fall of the world, practiced national salvation at their own posts. In the autumn of the 21st year of the Republic of China, they raised funds to found the Huada Handkerchief Factory in Hong Kong, equipped with new-style machines, and manufactured various handkerchiefs. It was also registered with the Chinese, British, and Philippine governments, using three sheep as its trademark. Although handkerchiefs seem like a small thing, they are actually a necessity of daily life. Society's ladies all have one in their hands. And when you trace its origins, they are all foreign goods. The products originally made in our own country were crudely made, and almost no one paid attention to them. Huada, on the other hand, uses the same machinery as foreign goods, extracts the strengths of others, and is based on scientific principles, striving for excellence. The raw materials are taken from our own country, so the goods are of good quality and low price, surpassing imported goods. Only four months after opening, sales have spread all over the world, and the factory's products are in short supply. Therefore, they are even more eager to improve. Since Hong Kong is located in a remote corner, it is only beneficial for promoting sales abroad. It is inconvenient to promote sales domestically. Moreover, in the midst of the current advocacy of national goods to save the country, it is not enough to resist imports and recover profit rights without strong capital and a large scale. It is particularly necessary to increase capital and reorganize into a limited company. After discussion and decision, expansion was immediately started. In addition to adding machines to increase production, a branch factory was established in Guangzhou to facilitate domestic sales. Since then, business has become more developed. Domestically, Huada is sold all over China. Abroad, it has a lively and prosperous situation in Southeast Asia, Little Luzon, Siam, Singapore, and other places. The factory is still not satisfied. On the one hand, it is working hard to promote sales. On the other hand, it is working hard to improve manufacturing, aiming at modernization. Therefore, the products have become increasingly exquisite in recent days. Since the increase in tax rates has increased the cost for those who purchase in the mainland, it inevitably affects sales. The factory did not hesitate to sacrifice profits and reduce the selling price to circumvent tariffs, and sales have increased as a result. In short, since the expansion and reorganization of the factory, the development of its business has made great strides. It is truly a vital force in resisting foreign goods. If other businessmen in our country have this enthusiasm and perseverance to engage in national salvation at their own posts, then the disappearance of foreign goods from our country's market is a matter of sincerity.

Children's Year in the Women's National Goods Year

— Shi Jihong

Almost everyone knows this... This year is the Women's National Goods Year and also the Children's Year. The Women's National Goods Year is to make our 200 million female compatriots abandon foreign goods and switch to national goods. This is certainly true. All the foreign perfumes, powders, and the most fashionable European and American woolen and silk fabrics on every modern lady, if converted into bullets at sixteen yuan per thousand, then five thousand bullets would be the bare minimum.

But then again, in this Women's National Goods Year, good mothers and virtuous sisters, in addition to using national goods themselves and in their families, must also work towards the future masters of the Republic of China. Nine out of ten of the things that children wear, use, and play with are bought for them by their mothers and sisters. If, in the current Women's National Goods Year, smart and kind mothers and sisters should not only use national goods as their priority for themselves and their families, but should also make an effort to buy and use national goods for their own children, and train them to use national goods, eradicating the inferior habit of loving foreign goods that has already been pre-existing in children's hearts, then not only will this Women's National Goods Year not be wasted in the present, but also for the children of my country in the future thousands of years, a foundation for loving and using national goods will have been laid in advance. This is really a major event in the Women's National Goods Year.

Finally, I must also contribute something, that is, many toys and daily necessities should be taught to children to make themselves, to do it themselves, so that they have the spirit of self-reliance and creation, and unyielding perseverance. If we work towards children in this way, this Women's National Goods Year will have real meaning. It is much better than just shouting slogans. I respectfully use two old sayings to end this article.

Better to act than to sit and talk.

Short Story

The National Goods Kissing Ceremony

— Zhang

Mr. Gu sat alone on the sofa, a cigarette in his mouth and the Shen Bao newspaper in his hand, reading the newspaper and smoking a cigarette by himself. His wife, Mrs. Xiuwen, also sat opposite him, silently reading a recently published ×× Weekly. The air in the living room was unusually quiet, only the clock on the wall was ticking.

[Alas! Chinese people really have no way. Last year was the National Goods Year, but not only did the promotion of the nation fail to show any special achievements, but it gave foreign goods a chance to sell well. According to the records in the newspaper... [The excess of imports over exports in the first half of last year was about 47,400,000 yuan, and the total for the year was about 90 million yuan. On average, each of us has to bear more than two yuan in foreign goods alone. Alas! How can we not be heartbroken to think of this situation? But, it is hateful that the general women still think of themselves as modern and buy foreign goods as much as possible, regardless of the crisis of the country, society, and nation, and specialize in making efforts to use foreign goods... We, the people who are engaged in the National Goods Movement and promote national goods to save the country, what else can we say about this situation besides deeply sighing for the future of the nation? ...] Mr. Gu's words were full of indignation. This indignant, oratory tone suddenly broke the silent air of the entire room and moved Mrs. Xiuwen as well.

[Indeed, what you said is not wrong at all. If China is always like this, if the Chinese people are always not enlightened, only selling and looking up to foreign goods and despising domestic goods, then the crisis in the future cannot be ignored. And we women's circles should also bear a large part of the responsibility for national goods, because most of the women are in control of the family's economy...] Mr. Gu's wife, Mrs. Xiuwen, followed her husband's words. At the same time, when she said [Most of the family economy is in the hands of women], she couldn't help but smile and blush on both cheeks. She looked at Mr. Gu, and Mr. Gu also smiled at her, because Mr. Gu's family economy was also in the hands of his wife, Mrs. Xiuwen!

[Even though that's the case, it's not easy to get the general women to wake up together, right? Therefore, our colleagues in the National Goods circles made a fierce decision to set this year as the Women's National Goods Year, preparing to specialize in doing the work of the Women's National Goods Movement in this one year. I think if the general women can have a common awakening, the National Goods Movement can be said to be half successful. Do you think that's right?]

[This year is the Women's National Goods Year? That's great. From today onwards, I will definitely be a propagandist for the Women's National Goods Movement, uniting the general sisters to use national goods together, to fulfill your painstaking efforts, and to shoulder my responsibilities. What do you think, is it worth implementing?]

[Of course, that's great. If you can stand on my front line and work together on the work of the National Goods Movement, then you will be worthy of being my wife, the wife of the National Goods Doctor, (Mr. Gu has the alias of National Goods Doctor). From now on, I will call you the National Goods Lady!]

Saying that, they couldn't help but smile at each other. In the midst of the smiles, Mr. Gu walked closer to his wife, held her waist, and deeply kissed a sweet, long kiss on Mrs. Xiuwen's face. It can also be said that [it was Mr. Gu and his wife's ceremony of swearing to strive for the National Goods Movement.]

Free Talk

[The Reason for Literal Translation]

— Zuo Yangling

I happened to read Ma Xulun's [Reading Notes,] and saw the following item...

Recently, in a notebook, there was a joke about translation, saying that the Chinese phrase [驰骋书丛] "galloping through the book forest" was translated by the English as [Riding a horse through the book piles, running back and forth.] This is due to literal translation. But there is also a real story about this. The Jin scholar Zhang Jun drafted an edict of amnesty for Emperor Xizong, which contained the phrases [顾兹寡昧] "Considering my ignorance" and [眇予小子] "I, the blind little one." The translator said [Lonely and without relatives, not understanding things,] [Blind child]. Emperor Xizong used a sword to cut off Zhang Jun's mouth and pickle it in minced meat.

I only heard from my elders when I was a child that it is wrong to lie to people. Those who lie will have their tongues cut out and their intestines drawn out when they die and go to the underworld. Today I understand that translating incorrectly can also lead to having two pieces of lip skin cut off and chopped into minced meat. I am also someone who occasionally dabbles in translation. Isn't that a very dangerous situation!

The above is the story of the Jin Dynasty. That translator was also the emperor's personal translator, so he suffered such a tragic fate. We don't need to worry today, more than seven hundred years later, when there is no emperor. But looking at the momentum of the translators who have been attacking [literal translation] or [hard translation] in recent years, it can be said to be fierce. If they one day have power in their hands, even if they don't take out the means of [using a sword to cut off the mouth and pickle it in minced meat], they will at least make [literal translation] or [hard translation] unable to exist.

Translating [驰骋书丛] "galloping through the book forest" as [riding a horse through the book piles, running back and forth], and translating [眇予小子] "I, the blind little one" as [blind child] This kind of translation is indeed laughable and hateful, but in my opinion, this is not [literal translation] or [hard translation]. This is like [milk road], but [milk road] is [smooth translation]. Mr. Ma Xulun gave such an example and said [This is due to literal translation], which is really wrong.

According to Mr. Lin Yutang, Pearl S. Buck's complete translation of "Water Margin" has been published. Mr. Lin is carefully proofreading it, and in the first few chapters, he has already found one mistake, which is to translate the [朝] "court" character in [仁宗朝] "Emperor Renzong's reign" into the [朝] "to visit" character in the English word [visiting]. This is also very laughable, but according to Mr. Lin, other than that, it is really well translated and very faithful. Moreover, Pearl S. Buck is hoping that Chinese readers will point out her mistakes so that she can correct them.

I think the attitude of translation 丨丨 whether he advocates [smooth translation] or [literal translation] [hard translation] 丨丨 should be like Pearl S. Buck. [It is better to be smooth and not faithful than to be faithful and not smooth] Although it is the opinion of a learned person, it is not entirely good after all. As for the critics, instead of pointing out one or two mistakes and spreading them as jokes, it is better to point out all the mistakes and call on the translator to correct them.

Talking About the Changing Colors of Maps

— Mu Mutian

Last year, I saw the supplement [Latest World Political and Economic Map] in the New Year's issue of the Japanese magazine [Kaizo]. In it, the land of our [Republic of China] was densely covered with large dots of various colors, saying that those dots represented the spheres of influence of the great powers. [Manchukuo] was of course the same color as Japan. Things always happen in pairs. The day before yesterday, a certain newspaper reported that the December issue of the American magazine [TheGoography] had a map attached to it that painted our four northeastern provinces in red, labeled them as Japanese territory (the same color as Japan), and printed the words [Manchukuo]; In addition, the Canadian Manufacturers Life Insurance Company published an advertising calendar with a world map, which painted Manchuria in red and our country in yellow.

I am not someone who discusses national affairs, but because [Manchukuo] is mentioned, I always feel a little personal pain. Now that I hear that the colors of the map are changing, I can't help but shed a few tears of an exile in my heart.

But I also feel that those who draw maps, although they have ulterior motives, are in some places worthy of our admiration. As the saying goes... [A bright person does not do secret things.] I think it is also admirable for someone who supports bandits and commits treason to be able to confess it himself. I don't like people who [shake things under a cover] the most. It is good for us that they express it frankly and clearly, so that we can be alert and clearly understand our position. And those who draw maps are even more worthy of our gratitude if they are standing on the position of exposing traitors. In short, the people of the Northeast have been slaves of a fallen nation for two or three years. This is a fact known to the world and tacitly approved by some people. They tell us clearly, which also saves us from having to doubt. We can see those colors on the map every day, so that we don't forget that we are being slaves of a fallen nation.

The people of our China must know why we have reached this point, and strive to seek a way to solve it. I think we can no longer hold on to the principle of [Don't wash your dirty linen in public]. It would naturally be good if we could overcome the disgrace of the family and revitalize the family's reputation early on. If we can't overcome it, and we just stick to the principle of not publicizing it, how can that help the matter?

We need to recover lost territory. What do we need that nominal territory for? If the Northeast is actually occupied by the Japanese, but the map is still painted in Chinese colors, what good is that to us? We want reality to match the name. How can we recover lost territory? This is the question that we must always consider.

The newspaper that published the above news added an editor's note at the end, saying... [Such illegal publications should be severely banned, and relations should be made with the relevant countries to prohibit them]. I think that as long as we recover the lost territory, there will naturally be no more maps of that kind without us banning or negotiating to prohibit them. As long as we completely drive out the forces of those ambitious invading countries, and we can truly be independent, then those colored dots will be cancelled even if we don't negotiate. But how can we do that? This is what we want to ask.

Silence

— Xu Fu

[Silence is the best expression of everything. Our whispers of love are not yet the ultimate achievement of love; our cries to heaven are not yet the expression of the greatest sorrow. The expression in these moments should be a fossil-like, dead silence.] These few words of Mr. Zhou Zuoren express the essence of sorrow and joy.

Mr. Yu Qie, in [The Face After Dinner], also has a good description of the ultimate love. He said, [The sweeter it is, the less visible; the truer it is, the less visible. The less visible, the sweeter; the truer, the more easily it melts, the more ardent.] [This is unclear, unseen, unseeable, unbearable. It shouldn't be seen, even though in this instant, the mind depicts goodness, truth, and beauty. Not only are true lovers like this, but even disguised lovers are like this. When movies depict the sweetness of love between men and women, they embrace, and the man either slightly raises his head or looks at the woman's hair, gently stroking her, never studying her face to face; and the woman is happiest when she closes her eyes, not only not looking at the other person, but not looking at anything at all.] This is the same view as Mr. Zhou.

The sorrowful side is no exception. When we hear loud wailing, we don't feel particularly uncomfortable; what we fear most is the low sobbing that comes from afar on a stormy night. The same is true of facial expressions; a face of great anger is not terrifying, but what makes us tremble is the fossil-like, expressionless dead silence. When a woman is wronged, she will cry bitterly. A good husband, besides comforting her, should probably let her cry to her heart's content. Once she has cried enough, the grievance will disappear. Because this crying is not real sorrow. It does no harm to health. On the contrary, wanting to cry but having no tears, wanting to cry but not daring to, that is the profound pain in the world. Also, consider resentment. The short-sleeved friends sitting in tea houses and taverns are not only more straightforward than those in long gowns, but their gratitude and resentment are also much shallower. They immediately become brothers with a word of agreement, but instantly turn hostile with two words of disagreement. However, once victory or defeat is determined, the hatred is also released, and they are still brothers and one family. Long-gowned friends are not like this. Even a small flaw will be repaid many times over, and on the surface, they are smiling, but their hearts are more sinister than sharp knives. So, true gratitude and resentment are revealed in plainness or smiles; when faces are red and breathless, they seem very serious, but the matter is forgotten after it is over.

Speaking of anger again. When anger makes one's hair stand on end and push up one's hat, it has naturally reached its peak. But when the hat falls to the ground, or one's anger subsides. The greatest anger is not when hair can push up a hat, but when one wears a thousand-pound stone cauldron on one's head, preventing the expression of anger and forcing it to turn into a cold protest.

Cold anger is true anger. We can find it on the faces of child brides in the past, apprentices in southern stores, maidservants, slaves in colonies, in short, on the faces of all slaves wearing stone cauldrons.

They all become silent, a fossil-like dead silence. But they are not dead, they are still resisting. A nation, a country's subjects sometimes fall into this state, and this is the greatest anger.

Wells' Prediction: A Chronicle of the Sino-Japanese War in 1935 (Continued)

— Meng Zhen

The actions of various countries to punish Japan were only made clear at this time. Not only were European and American armaments factories selling submarines and mines, but also the navies of various countries, under the guise of saving expenses, dismantled their new weapons into parts, transported them to Chile in South America, and then from Chile to Manila, and then secretly handed them over to China. The Philippine Islands, as a base for Chinese submarines, greatly threatened Japan's maritime traffic. Seeing this situation, Japan disregarded treaties and built more submarine bases on the South Sea Islands. The American fleet, to protect the neutrality of the Philippine Islands, concentrated on Guam, while Japanese warships concentrated on the Chinese seas to blockade the Chinese coast. At this time, although the Japanese-American war had not yet broken out, the situation in the Western Pacific was very tense. Because to prevent the transport of arms to China, in 1936, two American submarines were sunk by Japan in the Chinese seas. Japanese submarines also appeared near Guam from time to time. Then, in 1937, the United States and Japan engaged in an unofficial naval war in the Western Pacific.

However, neither country issued a declaration of war. Roosevelt II, as a result of the adventurous nature of his economic policies, found himself in dire financial straits. Japan was also doing its utmost to carry out an expedition to strike at the heart of China. At this time, American conservatives suddenly changed their minds and, in order to vent domestic discontent, also advocated declaring war on Japan. They advocated re-annexing the Philippine Islands. When Japan's Wuchang expedition failed, the argument for war against Japan in the United States became unstoppable.

This Japanese-American war was short and not the final decisive battle, so it is omitted. The encounter between the two countries in the Pacific only lasted two days, after which the Japanese side, running out of ammunition, finally retreated under cover of a smokescreen at dusk. Japan thus ceded the sea lanes to submarines, while the main fleet retreated to ports with torpedo facilities, because of a lack of supplies, it no longer appeared at sea. On the other hand, the American fleet took this opportunity to sail triumphantly to Manila and announced a naval victory.

At this time, the domestic situations in both Japan and the United States were deteriorating rapidly, making it difficult for both countries to continue the war. Therefore, this Japanese-American war ended without a decisive battle and without any treaty. Both Japan and the United States had to deal with social reforms due to their respective domestic collapses.

The following year, in 1940, the scene of the war shifted to the European continent. The result of this war was that the entire European continent was reduced to scorched earth. The records of that time have not been preserved at all. The only remaining war record in the world is the diary of a Japanese officer from the Wuchang retreat, but it is fragmentary and unsystematic. However, we can still imagine from it the horror of the burning and killing at that time, which is unbearable to read. This officer probably died in Kaifeng.

×　　×　　×

The above is Wells' dream about the war in the Far East. As for the predictions about the war in Europe, fortunately, they can be found in the original book, and the length here does not allow me to continue talking like this, so I will stop here. (End)

Selected News Notes

— Ye Zi

(1) The Story

Film star Hu Die was hired by the Nanjing Grand Theater to perform a stage play in Nanjing, which was extremely popular. On the 11th, the hotel where Hu was staying received a letter warning Hu Die, with a bullet attached. The content roughly stated that Hu Die, in North China, with a song and a dance, had ruined half of the country. Now she has come to Nanjing to be charming, and the people of Nanjing do not want to see this captivating face or hear this song of national destruction. If she lingers any longer, she will be shot with a similar bullet.

A reporter from a certain newspaper wrote a poem:

In Nanjing, there is a anti-traitor group, sending letters with bullets attached...

Quickly move to a peaceful land, to settle your old cases.

Leave Nanjing, Butterfly! Return, Butterfly!

The Shang dynasty was destroyed by Daji; the Zhou dynasty was ruined by Bao Si; the Qin... although there is no clear record in history, we also assume that he was ruined by women, which is probably not entirely wrong; and Dong Zhuo was indeed killed by Diao Chan.

Lady Huarui wrote a poem... The king raised the surrender flag on the city, how could I know in the deep palace? One hundred and forty thousand men laid down their armor, not a single one was a man.

Two Brothers (8)(9)

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

Everyone finally came out of the small room and onto the deck, which was crowded with people, porters, and sailors.

The steam in the ship's belly hummed, as if shivering with impatience.

"Goodbye," Roland kept saying hurriedly.

"Goodbye," Lierre replied, standing on the narrow bridge connecting the "Lorraine" and the dock.

He shook hands with everyone once more, and then his family walked away.

"Hurry, hurry, get in the car!" the father shouted.

A hired carriage was waiting for them to take them to the port, where Babagri had the "Pearl" yacht ready and waiting for them to set sail.

There was no wind that day; it was a dry and calm autumn day, and the polished sea surface was as cold and hard as steel.

Jean grabbed one oar, and Babagri took the other, and they both rowed together. On the breakwater, on both banks, and even on the granite railings, there were countless wriggling, clamoring crowds, waiting for the "Lorraine" to pass. The "Pearl" passed through these two waves of people and sailed out of the harbor in a moment.

Captain Bozire sat between the two ladies, holding the tiller and saying...

"You'll see, we'll be waiting right in its path, right there, right there."

The two rowers rowed as hard as they could to get as far away as possible. Suddenly, Roland shouted...

"Look, I see its masts and those two chimneys. It has left the dock.

"Row hard, boys!" Captain Bozire repeatedly shouted.

Roland's mother took her handkerchief out of her bag and put it to her eyes.

Roland stood holding the mast, reporting...

"Now it's heading to the harbor... it's stopped... it's moving again... it's hooked up to the tugboat... it's moving forward... great! It has entered the two banks... do you hear the audience cheering... great! ... The tugboat towing it is the "Le Poudeau" tugboat... I can see its bow now... look, look... good heavens, what a majestic ship! Good heavens! Look!"

Mrs. Luceme and Captain Bozire turned around; the two rowers also stopped rowing; only Roland's mother did not move.

The huge mail ship, towed by a pair of powerful tugboats that seemed as small as silkworms in front of it, slowly, majestically, left the harbor. The crowds of Le Havre, crowded on the shore, on the beach, and in the windows, were suddenly inspired by a patriotic heart, shouting madly, "Long live the Lorraine!" They cheered and applauded for this heroic departure, this birth of a beautiful daughter of the sea in the great coastal city. But the mail ship, once it passed through the narrow passage enclosed by two granite walls, finally felt free and immediately abandoned its tugboats, walking alone like a giant monster running on the water.

New F丰 洋行 reported on the 16th: The New York stock market continued to rise, but due to active profit-taking by bulls, the advance was very slow. Trading was still brisk. Foreign investors were also buying. Wall Street believes Roosevelt's declaration is exceptionally good because the government's reduction of the dollar's gold content is mostly clear, and there was no mention of inconvertible paper money. Therefore, speculators infer that such paper money will not be issued. The total volume of transactions for the day was 354,000 shares. (Wheat) down by slightly over one cent, a natural reaction after the high surge the previous day. It can be bought again if it falls further. (Cotton) Opinions diverge on the currency control policy. Future market trends may again follow the acreage reduction plan, but as cotton prices rise daily, the achievement of acreage reduction becomes increasingly difficult. Today, bulls took profits at high prices, and the market trend narrowed. The Stabilization Fund bought gold at a price of $34.45 per tael, up 3.9 cents. The Dow Jones index is listed below:

Yarn and Cotton

Weak Actual Sales Cause Yarn and Cotton to Decline

The yarn market weakened again because actual yarn sales are sluggish. Dealers from various provinces are showing little interest, and overseas cotton markets are also reacting downward, weakening sentiment. According to some, there are still 6,000 to 7,000 bales to be delivered this month, so the market is particularly weak. Further-out months are slightly tighter and more expensive, it is said.

Yarn Falls One Yuan This Month

The open of the Renbiao market saw falling American cotton and weak buying interest, with all months falling by 134 points. In the afternoon, news emerged that spot yarn transactions were not smooth, and the market remained weak, with all months falling another 3, 4, and 7 points. The total volume of transactions for the day was 6,600 bales. It was found that Taichang sold 400 bales, Shenji 550 bales, Yichang 400 bales, Xiesheng 400 bales, and Tongxing 450 bales. Changfeng bought 1,350 bales, Ren 150 bales, Dachang 300 bales, Tonghe 250 bales, and Yi 2300 bales. The closing prices are as follows:

Renbiao Closing Price Gain/Loss Account Balance March 1736 Down 839,130

January 1720 Down 1018,600 April 1775 342,450

February 1757 727,750 Total 127,950

Yarn Sales Total Just Over 400 Bales

The liquidation of spot yarn remains sluggish. It was found that dealers from various provinces bought a total of only 418 bales throughout the day. The market is stable. The purchase amounts for each province are as follows:

Shantou 120 Nanjing 12 Sichuan 100 Yunnan 20

Inland 156 Ningbo Guangdong 10

The cotton market is showing signs of reaction, and with American cotton falling, the yarn market is depressed, and factories are not buying much spot cotton. Therefore, sentiment is softening again. At the same time, profit-taking short positions are closing out. However, the Ningbo bulls have not completely exited the market, and they are still bullish. If foreign cotton turns downward, the cotton market may stabilize; otherwise, there will still be turmoil.

Zheng Biao Shows Slight Decline

The open of the Zheng Biao market followed the fall in foreign cotton, and buying households also fell, with all months falling by 1 to 1.5 points. In the afternoon, there was profit-taking by bulls, and all months fell by 0.5 to 1 point. The total volume of transactions for the day was 49,300 dan. It was found that Jifeng sold 3,200 dan, Dafu 1,000 dan, Zhenda 1,300 dan, Xinheng 5,100 dan, Yuanda 1,300 dan, and Yuanxingchang 3,900 dan. Renfeng bought 3,800 dan, Yichang 2,400 dan, Yifeng 1,900 dan, Xincheng 1,800 dan, and Yuanda 1,200 dan. Factory Demand Remains Low

The need for spot cotton is subdued, and factories are buying little. The source is estimated to be 700 bales of Yao cotton and 585 bales of Tong cotton. The spot prices are as follows:

Hankou Fine Velvet 41.00 Chongxin Factory Purchased 200 Pieces Sent to Factory

American Cotton Reacts and Falls

Yesterday, the American cotton market situation was that due to reduced buying and poor news from Liverpool, it reacted with selling and fell. As a result, spot prices fell by 5 points, and futures fell by 10 to 14 points. Liverpool cotton spot prices rose by 8 points, and futures rose by 5 to 7 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices rose by 3 points. The Bombay cotton market was firm at first, but then fell due to some hedging sales and profit-taking by bulls. As a result, Pingar fell by 7.5 points, Ormla rose by 2 rupees, and Bailoxi rose by 1.75 rupees. Original telegrams on the left. (16th telegram)

Grains

Biao Flour Sees Bulls Selling Off

After the opening of the flour market yesterday morning, the market for all months turned to a looser trend. Because the quotation for foreign wheat, Chicago, fell by about 34 points, and Canada fell by about 3 points, sentiment was already flat and weak at the opening. Furthermore, the major factories have been selling off a considerable number of long positions for this month, and the guest traders have little intention of buying far-out months, so the market is consistently looser, falling by 12 points or so compared to the previous day. By the afternoon opening, the market for all months had entered a sideways pattern. Near-term months were weak but stabilized because factories stopped selling. However, the Tianjin traders were selling off distant months, causing sentiment to weaken again. With the end of the year approaching, it is feared that it will have to be temporarily suspended. As a result, this month fell by 1.25 points compared to the previous day, February to April fell by 1 point, and May and June fell by 1.5 points.

Futures and Spot Wheat Markets Are Equally Quiet

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning, the market for all months softened due to the foreign wheat quotation falling by about 34 points. February and March fell by 23 points compared to the previous day, but trading was very light, and the rest were empty.

In the afternoon opening, this month only opened at one price and did not open again afterwards. February, March, April, and May were all empty. The June new wheat trading was still brisk, initially opening at 7.6 points, and then slightly better by 5 points due to some buying by inland traders. However, future transactions are difficult to develop due to settlement. The spot wheat has not been delivered because the factories have not moved. It is estimated that high-quality goods will have to open at around 1 point, it is said.

The Trends in the North and South Rice Markets Are Slightly Different

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, there were more than 40 sources (over 5,000 shi), with late rice accounting for about half. Although guest traders' bids were tight, the outflow of goods was still smooth. Middle-grade late rice showed potential, and high-quality rice mostly went to warehouses, so there was no gain or loss. It is estimated that a total of 3,000 packages went to the Gong traders and warehouses. Various local thick japonica rice shops were slightly more active, and the market color was slightly stronger. Du Yangjian rice did not fluctuate much, and Yin Bianyuan rice also showed potential.

(Shanghai North) Twenty-six or seven ships arrived from various routes. The outflow of various goods on the market was normal. White japonica, white yuan, foreign Du Port Jian, and early thin rice prices were flat and weak. Except for a small premium on Yin Yuan rice.

Guest Xian Rice Continues to Rise by 67 Points

Guangdong Province Resells Xiangjing Rice

Yesterday, the appetite of both local and guest traders for guest xian rice was active. There was not much arrival, and liquidation was very strong. The market was gradually improving. Yesterday, the Fujian traders were the most eager. Local and Ningbo traders also had good appetites. The sellers raised prices by 10 points, resulting in a 67-point increase compared to the inter-market price. The unified market purchased 700 packages of Hunan machine red rice from Fuzhou at a price of $6.625 to $6.525. 265 packages of brown red rice were priced at $5.55. 550 packages of Mingguang machine rice were priced at $6.45. Also, the Ningbo traders purchased 277 packages of early Jiangxi brown rice at a price of $5. 500 packages of Hunan machine oil and 200 packages of Mingguang brown rice were purchased by the Yong traders. Local traders purchased over 1,000 packages of Hunan machine oil at a price of $6.94 to $6.55, and over 200 packages of Mingguang brown rice at a price of $5.35. 100 packages of Wuhu machine yuan rice were priced at $7.5.

The Fujian traders' white Shanghai-Fujian shipping resumed, purchasing but the market there was furthermore, both were again shouting higher prices, unable to purchase, Fuzhou traders also came to the market yesterday to inquire, because their daily ships are open, probably there will be purchasing.

Yesterday, in addition to purchasing various xian rice, the local traders also repurchased 1,000 packages of machine-processed Jing rice from Yufeng Company of the Bang traders at a price of only $6.02. This price is cheaper than the market price because the rice was originally directly processed and packaged by the Guangdong provincial government in Hunan province. After being packaged in Guangdong, it did not suit the local market, so it was returned to Shanghai for sale, resulting in a slightly lower market price, which the local traders jointly purchased, it is said.

Yellow Soybeans Rise Sharply, Then Slightly Rebound

Yesterday, the soybean market suddenly changed. The market price was pressed down by a small 23 points. In reality, it had already seen a 20-point increase in the past four or five days. The day before yesterday, Fuzhou city suddenly increased prices by nearly a point, causing general goods to stubbornly insist on raising prices, so yesterday's market saw a sudden drop in buying interest from all traders. The entire city traded a total of five or six carts, estimated that local traders bought two carts of Zhengyangguan soybeans at a price opening at $3.6 to $3.5. Factories bought two carts of Yingzhou soybeans, pulling $3.43. One cart of Xinyangzhou soybeans, priced at $3.35. Inland traders bought 600 packages of Guide soybeans, doing $3.52 to $3.5. There were no inquiries for export. Sugar Market

Domestic Green Sugar Rises Again by 34 Points

Crude Granulated White Sugar Also Sees a Turnaround

Yesterday, the sugar market saw an increase in customs gold and a reduction in Dutch exchange rates, and the trend improved. The association's official price for No. 24 crude granulated white sugar ordinary goods was $19, a good starting price of 3 points, and high-quality goods were $19.1. Re-exported goods rose by 5 points to $6.35. Dutch red sugar rose by 5 points, No. 9 at $15.45, and No. 8 at $15.2, and re-exported goods rose by 4 points to $6.8. Taikoo sugar rose by half a point, B mark at $19.55, and CW mark at $19.4. Chaozhou green sugar's land price increased, and sales gradually became brisk. Yesterday, over 1,600 packages were opened, with Tizhuang green at $12.78 to $12.6, and second-grade at $11.8. The previous market rose by 3 points. Zhangdiao green opened over 100 packages at a price of $12, rising by 4 points. Zhenji's own factory's cotton white sugar did not change, No. 1 at $17.9, and the rest remained the same. Various factory ice sugar prices rose by 1 point, with No. 1 at $22.8 and No. 2 at $22.7. Metals

Metal Prices Soar

According to news from various foreign firms yesterday, metal prices have soared. Although there is no major trading among local firms in this port, the firmness of the market is incomparable to before. According to telegrams received, details are listed below for reference:

Three Da

Overview of Daily Necessities Market (3) Xinan

Too much has been said about vegetarian food, and it still hasn't been thoroughly explained. People might suspect that I'm promoting vegetarian restaurants. That's not right. However, coming back to the point, those who open vegetarian restaurants are all vegetarians and believers in Buddhism. However, when we go to vegetarian restaurants, we can't say that it's sincere. It's a common problem with various food shops, but they still "bully newcomers." If we ask a few great lay Buddhists, such as Mr. Wang, Huang, Xu, or Qu, perhaps it's by chance, but the dishes they eat seem to be a bit more special than usual. This is not surprising. Old customers should be treated better than new customers who come once or twice. However, since vegetarian restaurants are run by Buddhists, they should adhere to the principle of "Buddha's equality," without distinguishing between new and old, and treat everyone equally. Only then can they say that "meat-eaters are base," and vegetarians can truly eliminate "the view of self and others."

Taking this opportunity, I have a few more words to say, which is that vegetarian restaurants often use the names of meat dishes for their side dishes, adding the word "vegetarian" to distinguish them, such as vegetarian chicken, vegetarian duck, vegetarian ham, vegetarian smoked goose, and vegetarian shark fin. The intention of the people in the restaurant may be to attract meat-eaters to try them. But in my opinion, since one is wholeheartedly vegetarian, why not forget about meat? Why still use meat dish names for everything? Therefore, I remember a saying in the countryside that mocks vegetarians, saying that they "pretend to eat three Guan (vegetarian) and hope for sixteen." If vegetarian side dishes still use meat names, isn't that like "pretending to eat three Guan vegetarian"?

Let's turn our attention back to the food of the coolies. If one is a Buddhist, one should naturally recite "Amitabha Buddha," it's really too pitiful. However, I haven't seen people in the countryside, not even having a grain of rice bran to drink every day, bracing their chests and drinking the northwest wind. Compared to the coolies in Shanghai, they can be said to be in heaven, while the former are truly in a hungry hell. Sometimes, after eating, we go out for a walk on the road and often see young San, seeing the food carriers coming and going, carrying leftover food and scraps, and they all rush forward, without asking why, and dump all the vegetables and leftover rice in their dirty lead buckets and iron cans. After they get so much food, of course, they will offer it to the old San, and in addition to feeding themselves, they still have to sell the leftovers. Sometimes, walking past Mofang Street, you can see this situation. Moreover, Mofang Street has even opened several restaurants for this purpose, which can be said to be "coolie restaurants." The small dishes that these restaurants can sell are probably the things that everyone doesn't want to buy in the small dish market, as well as the leftovers and scraps from the guests of various restaurants, a hodgepodge of "Eight Treasures Harmony Dish" (this is the name I gave it). In addition, on the sidewalks of the Republic Road, there are also many "temporary cafeterias" for coolies. Also, at all rickshaw parking lots, there are Jiangbei women, one hand carrying a large white lead water jug, and the other hand carrying a bucket (or basket) of food. The water jug is filled with boiling water (or tea), and the bucket is filled with pancakes, fried dough sticks, and the like. The rickshaw pullers hold a pancake in one hand and a water bowl in the other, sitting on the rickshaw frame, eating to fill their stomachs after catching their breath. If a guest hires a rickshaw, they chew a few bites, pull the rickshaw, and run desperately. Where else is there a chance to chew?

Shanghai has already reached the point where it only pays attention to eating and playing. Every morning, you can see people dumping "dog food bowls," full buckets and loads, being carried out from various alleys. Inside, there is a lot of white rice, which is taken to feed pigs. Especially in many families, the maids and elder sisters often forget their original appearance when they come to the city and dump the leftover vegetables and rice from the day into the dog food bowls. They no longer think that a grain of rice from the field to your belly can be said to be full of hardships and not easy. I remember that a certain book recorded that when a certain prime minister was in power, the leftover rice and dregs were all discarded in the ditch and flowed out with the water. A certain monk saw this and couldn't bear it, so he picked it up from the ditch, washed it clean, trampled it dry, and used it as food, and there was still a lot left over. Later, the prime minister failed due to something, and his fields and houses were all confiscated by the government. He stayed in a monastery to eat. The monk still used the collected and stored things as food. The prime minister ate it with relish and asked where it came from. The monk told him the truth, and the prime minister was moved. Therefore, I think that if people in Shanghai think of the prime minister's end, eating what he used to discard with relish, the same person, the difference before and after is so great, they should also cherish food a little. (Continued from December 29th last year)

Talks

Effeminate Men of Letters

— Liu

Since ancient times, men of letters have mostly been physically weak. There are very few who "lay down their pens and join the army" to become valiant warriors. Therefore, in the eyes of heroes and brave men, men of letters are "like women," and the wise and foolish emperors often have so-called dwarfs who sing and dance for entertainment. These dwarfs are men of letters. Later, actors and court musicians, generation after generation, had talented individuals, but in reality, they had become cultural slaves, equivalent to the ladies of the inner palace. However, although Confucius recruited students and taught them, he was not really a man of letters. In addition to the classics, rituals, music, and archery, he also taught riding and archery. His student Zilu learned "eighteen martial arts" and was known for his bravery. When the Duke of Lu went to Ying to meet the Duke of Qi, Confucius even brandished his sword and stepped forward to protect him, shaking the world with his prestige. Later, from the Qin to the Han dynasties, "emphasizing literature and neglecting military affairs," men of letters became widespread throughout the world, only knowing how to wield their pens, not knowing how to use guns and swords. In the Tang Dynasty, Li Shimin selected a group of men of letters from the Hanlin Academy to form an opera troupe. The men of letters in the Pear Garden were equivalent to actors and court musicians. At this time, it was most fashionable for men of letters to be "like women." Therefore, men of letters have been effeminate since ancient times, and there is historical evidence to support this. "It has been like this since ancient times."

A Tianjin newspaper reported that the manager of the Cultural Bookstore in Neijiang, Sichuan, named Chuan Yunlian, is about forty years old, has studied in Japan, and has served as a middle school principal and teacher. He is knowledgeable and has the demeanor of a famous scholar. In recent years, he has dressed in women's clothing, applied powder and rouge, and dresses as a woman both at home and outside. The people of the whole city say that he is a "freak." I think that Mr. Fu, this "man of letters" from Sichuan, is "knowledgeable" and has "the demeanor of a famous scholar," probably because he is pained by the decline of the world and mourns the demise of the Three Ways. He is demonstrating in person, following the ancients. Those who say he is a "freak" are simply reactionary elements who are destroying cultural revival movements. In today's world, as long as the political, academic, and moral standards are the "national essence that has existed since ancient times," there is support from above and below, cultural revival is underway, and the country's prosperity and strength can be expected soon. Mr. Fu's "dressing in women's clothing and applying powder and rouge" also belongs to the "national essence and morality that has existed since ancient times" and should be commended to set an example, which is the way to love the country. Moreover, some people advocate that "this Mr. Fu, who wishes to be born as a woman, is quite worthy of emulation." The reason given is that "our country has the most men of letters, and throughout history, every instance of dynastic rise and fall has had self-proclaimed men of letters stirring things up, harming the common people. It is difficult to write about it all. If the men of letters of today all acted like Mr. Fu, putting on airs and applying powder and rouge, and could all become graceful and effeminate like Mr. Fu, then there would be no ambitious people or diehards who spread rumors or confuse the public and distort right and wrong. Everything would be stable and peaceful without the need for control." This makes the great undertaking of feminizing men of letters seem even more urgent.

Review of "The Righteous Servant and the Treacherous Friend"

— Ling He

Day of Reckoning

Generally speaking, ethical dramas easily evoke deep emotions in people. This is because everyone has a profound understanding of the relationships between fathers and sons, husbands and wives. Therefore, when comparing the emotions in the film with their own experiences, they often feel a sense of genuineness, assuming the author is truly rich in emotions.

In China, the [Humanitarianism] of "Humanity" (Rendao) can attract a huge audience, which is a clear example.

We sincerely say that the author of [Humanity] only presented outdated concepts in [Humanity], and [new interpersonal relationships] were not seen in [The Light of Motherhood]. Similarly, the author of [The Righteous Servant and the Treacherous Friend] only used extremely outdated understandings to deal with love and friendship, and even praised servants for their loyalty to their masters.

John Tam is imprisoned for debt and sentenced to two years in prison. His wife seeks help from her husband's friend, Holmes, due to the difficulty of supporting her husband and her livelihood. Holmes, driven by lust, secretly arranges for John Tam to be imprisoned and then seizes his wife. At this time, only the Tam family's maid does her best to take care of her two young masters. Soon, Tam's wife falls in love with Holmes and is shot to death by Holmes' other mistress. Holmes is also imprisoned. In prison, friends become enemies, and Tam eventually puts Holmes to death. After Tam is released from prison, he deeply thanks the maid.

The themes we explore in this story are: a wife who cannot share adversity and is unfaithful should die; one who commits adultery with a friend's wife should also die; and a loyal husband, even in danger, should be saved. As for loyal servants, they should naturally have a good outcome. The author is trying to maintain the existence of old moral ethics, especially by adopting the method of karmic retribution to end the lives of each character in the play, which feels even more fragile and mediocre.

From a new perspective, economic circumstances dictate everyone's behavior. Adultery with a friend's wife cannot be resolved by morality alone. In particular, a wife's weakening awareness due to life's hardships and her transfer of affection to another man is not a particularly serious crime. As for writing about the maid doing her best to support the master's children, it evokes a sense of alienation.

I think the most brilliant part of the author's treatment of this story is the sincerity of friendship in prison used to resemble Holmes, which is a relatively appropriate method.

In terms of performance, the director's biggest lack is insufficient emotion. In some cases, we are against unnecessary sentimentality, but the director, Charles R. Brabin, has not emphasized the emotional component under such an outdated theme, which shows that his creativity is indeed insufficient.

In addition, the director is clear and smooth in organizing the story. What is more commendable is that he does not excessively exaggerate Holmes' ugliness. He allows the other characters to develop naturally. No, to be precise, he does not write about the so-called bad being excessively bad, nor does he make the so-called good excessively sympathetic. This naturally does not use dramatic exaggeration; otherwise, the exaggeration will strengthen the poison of old ideas. Saying this seems to be the benefit of insufficient performance methods. A smile.

There are several scenes that should be specifically pointed out. When John Tam sees his child through the prison window, he cries out in sorrow and joy: "He can already walk, he already..." In addition, when John Tam learns of his friend's shamelessness in prison, he exclaims, "He is my friend!..." followed by mad laughter. All of this is where the director excels.

The protagonist, Richard Dix, did indeed perform very well in the above two scenes. However, that is his only merit, and the rest is very mediocre. Among the supporting actors, none are particularly lovable, but Una Marke, who plays the maid, is relatively natural.

Regarding Richard Dix, he does not seem to be frequently seen by Chinese audiences. As far as I know, he starred in many films, including [The Sin Flood], [Glorious Fool], [Souls for Sale], [The Price of Glory], [The Ten Commandments], [Happiness Ahead], [Man Must Live], [The Christian], [Nothing to Lose], [The Sporting Lover], [Young Nowheres], [The Great Divide], etc. Many of them have not come to China. [The Ten Commandments] left the deepest impression.

Regarding this film, if I were to write a few general comments, it should be that it is neither good nor bad, a film at the level of old-fashioned works.

New Film Production at Lianhua Third Factory

[Return] (Gui Lai), written and directed by Zhu Shilin of Lianhua Third Factory, was shown at the Capital Cinema in Nanjing, where it was full every day and received excellent reviews. Now, this film has been acquired by the newly built Jincheng Grand Theater in Shanghai for its Shanghai premiere. The new film produced by the factory after [Return] is [A Beautiful Night] (Liang Xiao), written by Zhu Shilin and directed by Yang Xiaozhong. At the same time, in order to increase production and meet social needs, two comedies are being filmed. One is [Seeking a Spouse] (Zheng Hun), starring the fat Yin Xiucen, and the other is a script written by Shen Aijuan, tentatively named [Street People] (Jie Tou Ren), a collaboration between Liu Jiqun and Han Langan. [Seeking a Spouse] is light and clever, and quite interesting. [Street People] is a tear-stained comedy. The characters in the play are two wanderers, an orphan, and a grandmother who makes a living by doing laundry, as well as a landlord and the landlord's maid. Because these two comedies are extraordinary, they are special productions of the Third Factory and will create a new record for domestic comedy films.

Director Sun's Selection of New Talents

It is undeniable that the Chinese film industry lacks talent in all aspects. Lianhua is the company that pays the most attention to cultivating new talents, and Sun Yu is the first person in Lianhua to particularly work hard to select talents. In his recent work, [Sports Queen] (Tiyu Huanghou), he scouted Zhang, who had been stuck in a small company for a long time, as the male lead. For the female leads, he gave Wang Moqiu and Wang superior positions so that they could develop their talents. He also selected two female actors, Yin Xu and Bai Lu, who had never been on camera before. Although these two new talents had never been on camera, their innate acting talents were instructed and enlightened by the director, and their brilliance began to show. The impression left on the film is very good. According to Director Sun, they will definitely be a sensation. Although it is not an exaggerated praise of some kind of new discovery, it is undoubtedly that they will gain a superior position among actors in the Chinese film industry in 1934. Let's wait and see.

Fat Yin Xiucen Wins First Prize

During the sale of aviation lottery tickets, almost everyone had to buy at least one strip. It doesn't cost much, but there is a chance to get rich and help with aviation construction. Why not do it? Therefore, the sales of lottery tickets are very enthusiastic every period. The colleagues at Lianhua, of course, have to buy them too. When the third period was drawn, although some only got the last digit of the first prize, everyone was not disappointed but smiled happily.

A few days after the drawing, Yin the Fat hurried to the first factory. But he ran over in a hurry, and when he talked to Fei Mu, he secretly fumbled around as if he had a secret. Soon, the news that Yin Xiucen had won the first prize spread. Of course, everyone wanted to see his lottery ticket, and immediately everyone looked at him with special eyes and asked him to treat them, but he did not admit it. But finally, everyone saw his lottery ticket. Indeed, it was 313817. When people surrounded him and asked him to treat them, he burst out laughing. It turned out that he had cut and pasted the numbers of this first prize from lottery tickets next to him. Everyone looked closely and realized that they had indeed been fooled by the fat man.

Movie Novel

The Cat and the Fiddle (9)

— Mo Chen

Victor said in dismay, "If you don't let your wife go on stage, won't the show be a disaster?" Odette's husband said, "Show? It's over." He turned back to Odette and said, "How is it? Have you thought about it? But you have to know that no matter what you want, I will never invest in that show again." Odette looked embarrassed. She thought that if her husband didn't pay, the show wouldn't succeed. She really wanted to return to the stage and enjoy the glory of success, but if she failed, what would there be to enjoy? So, this Odette, who was used to comfort and luxury, had to surrender. She said to her husband, "What's wrong, my love? Of course, I'll go with you."

Victor watched them leave. Money is omnipotent. The old man was even more confident in his boundless power, because at this time Odette had already taken his arm, leaning tightly against him, her beautiful face turned up to him with a charming smile. After they left, Victor felt that his success had disappeared like a dream, and with it the hope of winning Sherry. After a while, he suddenly mustered his courage again and decided to fight to the end. He gathered all the actors and rehearsed again. He instructed his assistant to immediately find a female lead, telling him to search all of Paris and find her, because his operetta must be performed tomorrow!

By the next morning, the whole city of Paris was talking about this as a new joke. And someone told Sherry about it, and told her that not only had the female lead left, but the male lead had also run away. Therefore, he is now doing the male lead himself and needs to find another female lead. And since Odette's husband is unwilling to pay any more money, the show will have no hope of success. Also, the theater side... The theater owner was originally going to guarantee it. Victor gave him a promissory note. So, if Victor's show fails, he will not be able to cash that promissory note, and he will have to go to jail. Therefore, his current situation is really very dangerous. After Sherry heard this, she said coldly, "That's none of my business. I really don't want to hear about Victor anymore." After the guest left, Sherry ran around the room alone, really worried about Victor. Then she realized that she still loved him... even more than before.

The curtain is about to rise. The Cat and the Fiddle is about to take the stage. Behind the curtain, a large group of actors huddled together. Victor was also squeezed in with them. The newly found female lead stared at him with tears in her eyes. She said, "In the past, I could perform as I pleased. Now I am old. Do you think a grandmother can still go on stage and play a young girl?" Victor patted her on the shoulder, comforting her and saying, "My love, it doesn't matter, you will definitely perform very well, don't worry." Although he said so, his heart was already half cold. He thought of the mockery of him all over Paris tomorrow... everyone mentioning his name, his operetta, and his ridiculous female lead... tomorrow... he smiled coldly with his mouth twisted... tomorrow, wouldn't he already be locked up in jail because he couldn't cash that check? But time did not allow him to think deeply alone, his program had arrived, and he had to go on stage, and he had to perform well... (To be continued)
